Cai Zengji, General Manager of the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, Encourages Employees to Fulfill Their Responsibilities: Currently Undergoing Reorganization, Hoping for Mutual Encouragement to Develop Domestic and Foreign Routes and Recover Profits 111

Since Cai Zengji took over as General Manager of the State-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, he has been determined to reorganize the company and has spared no effort. All reorganization plans have been implemented in order. Cai issued a notice to encourage employees the other day, which is excerpted below: "Since the reorganization of this bureau, various

reorganization plans

have been promulgated by the Ministry of Transportation and implemented accordingly. However, at the beginning of the reorganization, the original intention of all facilities may not be fully understood. Therefore, I would like to sincerely express my thoughts to my employees, who share weal and woe with me. In the international competitive environment of the 20th century, any country that can survive relies entirely on active policies and active implementation. The so-called active is just like what the sages said, 'burn the boats and break the pots,' and what President Chiang said, 'hard work' and 'bitter work.' If you try to look at Italy’s recent years of enhancing its national status, and Germany’s restoring its lost authority, both are using the implementation of active policies as the only effective weapon. Our country is very weak and it is more than necessary to save it from its current dangers. This bureau is a state-run shipping agency and is responsible for river and sea transportation, which is related to the lifeline of transportation. This time, the Ministry of Transportation, in accordance with the order of the Executive Yuan, is determined to reorganize this bureau, which is actually a part of implementing the government's active policies to save the country from its dangers. This bureau has now followed the order to cancel all

contracting systems

for all river steamers from April 1st. In the future, the reorganization of wharves, warehouses, real estate, and other ships will continue to be implemented. All patriots, aware that the affairs of this bureau are

related to the safety of the country,

should know to obey government orders and rise up to assist in order to realize the reorganization plan. The employees of this bureau are all part of the nation, and their clothing and food are even more closely related. They have the responsibility to obey and implement the order. In the notice issued by President Chiang of the Executive Yuan on the reorganization of this bureau, it says, 'The Executive Yuan has ordered the Ministry of Transportation to reorganize the bureau, amend the organizational regulations of the bureau, and instruct on reorganization methods. The intention is to completely eliminate and clear out the long-standing malpractices of harming the public for personal gain and procrastination and perfunctoriness. If such measures are not thoroughly reformed, it will be understood and accepted by those who understand reason. The staff of the bureau have been serving in the bureau for a long time and are familiar with the situation. Regarding how to eliminate the long-standing malpractices, how to improve the business, and how to increase income and reduce expenditure, if there are any insights, they can be fully presented to their superiors for adoption. If they do not

follow the proper procedures

and insist on their own private opinions, or even be seduced by bad elements from the outside world, sow discord, and instigate disturbances, causing the bureau's business to be affected, the president will regard it as a violation of discipline and destruction of transportation and will strictly enforce the law and will not tolerate it in the slightest. In addition, if employees in branch offices and warehouses and docks have such behavior, they should also be punished equally.’ I, all employees in office, have long understood this deeply, and can each be able to do their duty, cooperate, and jointly plan for progress, to complete their mission, so as to directly seek the interests of the majority of people, and indirectly seek the wealth and strength of the country. Those who are used by others, and seek personal gain, regardless of the interests of the country, deliberately obstruct progress, this bureau, even if it wants to be lenient, will not be allowed by the law. This bureau firmly believes that most employees are able to understand righteousness and do not need further instructions. However, if there are a few who do not understand the truth, all employees should, based on their personal responsibilities, turn to enlightening them, and work together to achieve success. If they do not follow the enlightenment, they should immediately report to the主管 personnel for investigation and handling. Furthermore, the bureau has been established for more than 60 years, and to this day the tonnage of ships is only more than 70,000 tons,

the scope of the routes

is only domestic, to the north and south oceans, and the upper and lower reaches of the Yangtze River. If you try to compare it with the Japan Mail Ship Company of Japanese merchants, which was established two years after the establishment of this bureau, the tonnage of ships has reached more than 770,000 tons, and even as far as Europe and the United States, as well as India, Australia, South America and other places, there are its routes. Compared to this bureau, one cannot avoid being too

harsh.

The reason why the Japan Mail Ship Company has developed day by day is that it relies on the people of the whole country to support and help each other, and the joint efforts of the employees, which has created an unparalleled career. The past history of this bureau will not be detailed here. Now it is not too late to mend the fold even after a sheep has been lost. From now on, we will gradually reorganize, increase the tonnage of ships, fully expand domestic routes, recover the lost profits, and in the future, extend the routes to the Nanyang Islands, where overseas Chinese reside, and to places such as Little Luzon, relying on the sincere patriotism of enthusiastic people across the country to support and help each other, so as to realize it. But how to start implementing it is the responsibility of all the employees in the bureau, which cannot be emphasized enough

with diligence and mutual encouragement,

in order to fulfill their responsibilities. I am willing to encourage this with all the employees in office, and hereby announce it. Cai Zengji, General Manager of the State-run China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, April 1, 25th year of the Republic of China.

Zha Pu Mountain Opened for Three Days 112

Fellow Zha Pu people traveling in Shanghai received news from home yesterday, saying that Zha Pu residents sweeping tombs on the mountain has now been approved by the local garrison commander, with the period of the 4th, 5th and 6th of this month, after which entry and exit is not allowed.

Special District Rickshaw Merchants Still Suspended Business Yesterday; Rickshaw Pullers Clashed with Police Due to Forcibly Seizing Vehicles; Deflated Rickshaw Pullers Have Been Sentenced Separately by the Court; Mutual Aid Society Decides to Issue Relief Funds During the Suspension Period 113

Rickshaw merchants in the special district, protesting the reduction of rickshaw rental fees by the Public Works Department, have collectively stopped operating their vehicles since April 1st, effectively staging a market strike. Yesterday, the merchants continued their suspension, and rickshaw pullers, pressured by their livelihoods, demanded the release of the vehicles, leading to disturbances. The rickshaw pullers' mutual aid society convened in the afternoon to discuss relief measures for the pullers. Party and government authorities dispatched personnel to thoroughly investigate the truth. Deflated rickshaw pullers were sentenced separately by the court yesterday. The details of each situation are recorded separately below:

Continued Suspension

At 9:00 PM the night before last, the Special District Rickshaw Guild convened an emergency cadre meeting due to the Public Works Department Board of Directors' refusal to reduce the rickshaw rental fees. Attendees included Yin Zhiling, Hou Shao'an, Gu Songmao, and others. During the meeting, Yin Zhiling first reported on the petition process. After discussion, based on the opinions of the rickshaw pullers and merchants, it was decided to continue the struggle until a resolution was reached to achieve their demands. Therefore, it was resolved that the strike would continue on the 2nd. (New Voice Society)

Demand to Release Vehicles

Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, rickshaw pullers from various districts held a meeting at the mutual aid society on Jiaxing Road. It was decided to petition the rickshaw merchants' mutual aid society and the Ratepayers' Association, demanding the release of vehicles for business. They first went to the residence of rickshaw owner Yin Zhiling to negotiate. Then, at 10:00 AM, they sent representatives, including Hou Debiao and five others, to petition the Rickshaw Committee. Chairman Massey received them and promised to find a solution. They then went to the Ratepayers' Association to make the same petition. More than a thousand rickshaw pullers also went to the mutual aid societies on Maigen Road and Beile Road to request relief. (New Voice Society)

Conflict Erupted

Yesterday morning at 7:00 AM, about fifty rickshaws belonging to rickshaw owners such as Xu Songxi were hidden in empty houses on Xietu Road and Father Du Road. Rickshaw pullers found out and gathered over a hundred people to demand the release of the vehicles. However, the guards refused to release the vehicles without the owners' consent. The rickshaw pullers shouted, "If we don't work for a day, we have nothing to eat. Our families will starve!" This led to a dispute, and the rickshaw pullers seized the vehicles and fled. During the chaos, the guards were beaten and injured. The relevant Chinese Concession police authorities dispatched a large number of officers to the scene to suppress the situation, preventing further accidents. The owners recorded the numbers of all seized vehicles and reported them to the Rickshaw Guild, which sent personnel to investigate on various roads. At around 9:00 AM on the same morning, over five hundred rickshaw pullers gathered near Jumen Road in the Nanshi district and flocked to the Liyuan Road No. 39 Rickshaw Company, demanding the release of vehicles. The company refused to release the vehicles, citing the industry's decision not to do so until a satisfactory solution was reached, leading to a conflict. Sha Bingming, a police officer stationed at the Jumen Road police station of the Ximen Branch, went to investigate due to the large number of people, which led to a misunderstanding and he was beaten by the rickshaw pullers. He was sent to Shanghai Hospital for treatment by ambulance. Subsequently, patrol officer Zhang Shaoqin noticed the situation and went to mediate, but was also mistakenly beaten, although his injuries were not serious enough to require hospitalization. Upon receiving the news, the Ximen Branch dispatched over forty officers, led by Branch Chief Yao, to suppress the situation. The rickshaw pullers then flocked to the Southern District branch of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society. At this time, the French Concession police sent a large number of detectives to stop them, leading to another conflict. Rickshaw pullers Xu Housheng, Xu Hejin, and Wang Cilin were injured, with Xu Housheng being the most seriously injured. The French Concession police dispatched over fifty Chinese and foreign detectives and special patrol officers to patrol the area. The Chinese territory also dispatched dozens of officers to maintain strict vigilance to prevent further conflicts. (New New Society)

Preserving Empty Vehicles

Around noon yesterday, about five thousand rickshaw pullers from the northern and southern cities went to various rickshaw leasing agents and pulled empty vehicles into the concession. However, most owners had deflated the tires or stored the cushions, so the rickshaw pullers were unable to operate, even though they had pulled them into the concession. Therefore, they dragged them to various police stations for storage. By 5:00 PM, the Gordon Road Police Station had over a thousand vehicles, and the Avenue Road Police Station had over five hundred vehicles. Other police stations also had vehicles dragged in for storage. According to police officials, since the rickshaw pullers could not operate the vehicles after pulling them into the concession, they feared theft and disputes, so they instructed the rickshaw pullers to drag them to the police stations for temporary storage. The vehicles would only be returned after the owners had provided proof to the police station. (Ta Kung Society)

Seizing Vehicles in Zhabei

Between 2:00 PM and 4:00 PM yesterday, at the Qin Mingde Rickshaw Company in Fuyuan Lane, Wuzhen Road, Zhabei; the Li Xichun Rickshaw Company on Wuzhen Road; the Liu Guiji Rickshaw Company in Yuchang Zu Lane, Xinjiang Road; the Wang Lianji Rickshaw Company in Huazhen Fang, Xinjiang Road; the Feixing Rickshaw Company operated by Gu Songmao at the intersection of Guoqing Road and Xinmin Road; and the Feixing Rickshaw Company in Feixing Lane, Xinmin Road, about a thousand rickshaw pullers forcibly seized and pulled rickshaws from these companies. Their reason was that they were "daily-wage coolies" who could not live without pulling a rickshaw for a day. This was learned by Cui Hu, a patrol officer from the Wuzhen Road police station of the Xinzha Branch, who immediately led officers Wu Dengxin, Hu Yao, and others to suppress the situation and maintain order. He persuaded the companies to release the vehicles, and the disturbance was quelled. The Xinzha Branch, upon hearing the news, ordered the deputy leaders of the detective squad, Bao Ziying and Shi Zuhan, to lead detectives Sun Youzhi and others to assist at the scene. The Detective Division of the Municipal Public Security Bureau also sent detective Yu Liangzhi to investigate the incident and report the situation. Officer Cui of the Wuzhen Road police station, fearing further unexpected incidents, issued a strict order stating that the police station bore a major responsibility for suppressing and maintaining order during the rickshaw puller disturbance, and that no officers were allowed to leave their posts.

Rickshaw Puller Petition

At 9:30 AM, rickshaw pullers held a temporary meeting at the mutual aid society. After discussion, they decided to insist on three demands and continue to petition the Rickshaw Committee of the Upper Public Works Department and the Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession, requesting assistance to force rickshaw merchants to reduce rental fees and release vehicles for business in order to maintain their livelihoods. They elected Tan Zhengyu, Hou Debiao, Chen Naicun, Gao Yongquan, and others as representatives to petition the Public Works Department at 10:00 AM. Chairman Massey of the Rickshaw Committee received them and expressed his acceptance of their demands, instructing them to strictly observe public order and seek assistance from all parties through peaceful means. The representatives were satisfied and left. They then petitioned the Ratepayers' Association, which also promised to provide assistance. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the rickshaw pullers held another meeting at the mutual aid society, resolving to organize a representative petition group to petition the Municipal Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, the Social Affairs Bureau, the Chinese Ratepayers' Association, and the Citizens' Federation at 10:00 AM today. (New New Society)

Party and Government Relief

A public document from the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society Rickshaw Pullers' Council and He Wushan stated that yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM, they specially met with rickshaw puller representatives Xia Huaixiang, Zhu Fengxiang, Yang Xingyou, Ji Decai, and over one hundred and twenty others, and went by car to the Municipal Party Headquarters at Fenglin Bridge to petition. The Municipal Party Headquarters dispatched Zhang Sheng, a cadre from the People's Movement Section, to receive them. After inquiring about the purpose of the petition, he promised to forward the situation to higher authorities for review. The representatives were satisfied and went to petition the Municipal Central District Social Affairs Bureau. The bureau dispatched Zhang Chuqiang to receive them, stating that the authorities had already been informed of the situation yesterday and would handle it quickly after preparing proper measures. The representatives were satisfied and returned. The Social Affairs Bureau dispatched Wang Gang, director of the Welfare Industry Section of the Third Division, to the trade association and various parties to investigate the truth. The Municipal Party Headquarters, based on the rickshaw pullers' petition, also dispatched personnel to investigate the process in order to discuss solutions. (New Voice Society)

Admonishing Rickshaw Merchants

On the afternoon of April 2nd, the French Concession Police Department summoned several important public rickshaw merchants within the concession, numbered from 1 to 10,000, for a discussion. The police urged the merchants to pay close attention to the special nature of the suspension of rickshaw rentals since the 1st of this month and the livelihoods of the tens of thousands of rickshaw pullers and their families affected by the event. They were urged to resume business as soon as possible so that the unsustainable situation caused by the merchants' suspension could be stopped immediately. The merchants promised to pay each currently unemployed rickshaw puller two dimes per day to maintain their livelihoods and compensate for the losses incurred during unemployment.

Warning to Rickshaw Owners

According to a Public Works Department Intelligence Office report, a spokesman for the Public Works Department Rickshaw Affairs Committee stated that since public rickshaw owners had declared a suspension of business to resist the Public Works Department Board of Directors' proposed reduction of rickshaw rental fees, the Rickshaw Committee intended to suspend the reissuance of some of the existing licenses. The type of licenses subject to suspension would depend on whether the owner was a leader in the dispute and whether they were adamant about suspending vehicle operations. Therefore, the Rickshaw Committee had to earnestly warn all rickshaw owners to promptly claim their April licenses and immediately release their vehicles. Those who heeded the warning would have the least opportunity for reconsideration.

Emergency Relief

Since all rickshaw pullers of the Rickshaw Pullers' Mutual Aid Society were members, the society was concerned about the future if this situation continued. The society convened a special meeting of the board of directors at 5:00 PM yesterday (April 2nd). Ten directors attended, as well as Zhang Deng, the general director of the mutual aid society, and Chen Chunbao, the deputy general director. Chairman Massey reported on the need to implement emergency mutual aid to maintain the livelihoods of the unemployed members. The following key points were unanimously approved: Each member would be given one dime and five cents per day. To avoid overcrowding, they would receive three dimes every other day. When more than half of the vehicles in the Public Concession were operating again, this mutual aid would be suspended. Although the amount of money issued daily was substantial, the society believed that the matter was very important to the livelihoods of the rickshaw pullers, so they would find ways to maintain it no matter what. The one dime and five cents per day per person was determined based on the opinions collected from various members in recent days.

Court Trial

Yesterday morning around 6:00 AM, Mao Guoshu and Jiang Deyuan, both from Jiangbei, rented two British Concession rickshaws from Shi Changyuan and Cao Wangao at No. 3, Zhunshun Lane, Puenjishi Road. However, Zhao Yong'an and Qian Xuen, both from Dongtai, stepped forward, blocked their way, and prevented them from pulling the rickshaws, taking away the seat cushions. Patrol Officer No. 655 of the French Concession Police reported this to the police station, and Detective Liu Jinrong was dispatched to arrest Zhao and Qian, who were sent to the First Special District Court in the afternoon. The police lawyer stated that the police were prosecuting the defendants based on the Law of Remote Justice. When questioned, Zhao and Qian confessed that they had prevented the pulling of the rickshaws but had not used violence. Judge Qiu ordered Zhao and Qian to each pay a fine of five dimes as a warning.

Public Concession police personnel apprehended many perpetrators of tire deflation the day before yesterday. The Chengdu Road Police Station apprehended thirteen people, the Laozha Police Station apprehended four, the Xinzha Police Station apprehended five, and the Gordon Road Police Station apprehended seven. The Hudong Yulin Road and 思威路 Police Stations also apprehended eighteen. In total, over forty people were apprehended. Yesterday morning, according to the jurisdictions of each police station, they were separately sent to the First Special District Court's Second and Fifth Criminal Courts. Police lawyers Qian Xunjiu and Jiang Baolian filed a public prosecution based on Article 304 of the Criminal Law, accusing them of the crime of obstructing freedom by using violence and coercion to force people to do things they had no obligation to do or interfering with people's exercise of their rights. After questioning by Judges Ye Shengchao and Yang Qianchang, the deflation perpetrators were sentenced to fifteen, twenty, and thirty days of detention respectively as a warning.

Guild Statement

The Special District Rickshaw Guild issued a statement, stating that rickshaw owners and rickshaw pullers have a close relationship of mutual dependence and coexistence in both business and life, which is not a simple leasing relationship. However, after the establishment of the Rickshaw Committee two years ago, it was believed that the leadership of the rickshaw pullers should not belong to the merchants, but should be led by the mutual aid society, with the Rickshaw Committee being responsible for it. The rickshaw merchants protested, but to no avail. The Rickshaw Committee then organized rickshaw puller registration, and all rickshaw puller issues were under the supervision of the mutual aid society. This time, the Rickshaw Committee enforced new regulations and forcibly collected mutual aid fees. The rickshaw pullers, based on their own interests, declared their refusal to pay the mutual aid fees, which was not allowed by the Rickshaw Committee. The rickshaw merchants had no choice but to temporarily suspend business and await a resolution. As for the livelihood issue of the rickshaw pullers after the suspension, it was initially thought that since the leadership of the rickshaw pullers belonged to the mutual aid society and the mutual aid society had collected a large amount of membership fees from the rickshaw pullers, amounting to 300,000 yuan, the society would be able to comprehensively plan and provide effective relief for the livelihood of the rickshaw pullers after the suspension, which was its obligatory task. However, judging from the society's actions in the two days since the suspension, it had not made any statement regarding the issue of maintaining the livelihoods of the rickshaw pullers, and had even led and directed the rickshaw pullers to engage in various excessive and destructive behaviors. According to statistics from various police stations, hundreds of incidents of disturbing order had occurred in the past two days. The guild deeply felt that if this continued, it would be concerning for social security and the livelihoods of the rickshaw pullers. In addition to trying to remedy the situation within its possible scope, the guild stated that the rickshaw pullers' actions were led by the mutual aid society and the Rickshaw Committee, and the rickshaw merchants were not involved. It feared that the outside world would not understand the truth and therefore made this statement. (New Voice Society)

Chamber of Commerce Official Letter

The Shanghai Chamber of Commerce sent a letter to the Public Works Department requesting a proper solution. The original text stated: "To the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department: On April 1st, we received a letter from the Shanghai Rickshaw Trade Association Special District Office stating that the Rickshaw Committee suddenly notified all rickshaw owners on March 31st that it would implement new regulations from April 1st, implementing rental fee reductions and forcibly paying mutual aid fees, otherwise licenses would be revoked. The association's rickshaw owners have informed the rickshaw leaders, but the rickshaw pullers have refused to pay the mutual aid fees based on legitimate reasons, and the Rickshaw Committee is forcibly collecting them with authority. The rickshaw owners are in a dilemma, and even if they continue business as usual, they are bound to suffer heavy losses, and are at risk of being fined heavily and having their licenses revoked. Therefore, all vehicles have been forced to stop operating, and the livelihoods of national business rickshaw pullers are in dire straits. The situation is urgent and the future is worrying. In addition to continuing to negotiate with the Public Works Department based on reason, we specially present the true situation and request an investigation. We sincerely ask for prompt assistance to maintain the livelihoods of hundreds of thousands of people." It was reported to the association that after the rickshaws stopped operating, the rickshaw pullers lost their jobs, which was bound to affect social security. We request that your bureau quickly formulate relief measures and immediately convene representatives of rickshaw merchants to discuss a solution to prevent the situation from escalating. This is our sincere hope. (New Voice Society)

Foreign Newspaper Report

The *North China Daily News* reported: "A representative of the *North China Daily News* visited an official at the Shanghai Public Works Department General Office yesterday (April 1st). It was stated that the petition submitted by the Rickshaw Guild last week had been transferred to the Rickshaw Committee for consideration. The committee is expected to submit its decision to the Public Works Department Board of Directors within a week. Whether the Public Works Department will negotiate with the owners depends on the nature of the committee's decision. As for the national owners' request to postpone the reduction of rental fees by 7.7 cents while the dispute is unresolved, it should be known that this new rental fee was decided after much consideration and the owners were notified well in advance. It is remembered that when the rickshaw fee was revised last year, the national owners also made the same objection at the last minute and requested an extension to continue negotiations. The owners claim that the current rental reduction violates the contract signed between the owners and the Public Works Department in August of last year, which stipulated a rental fee of 8.5 cents. The speaker believes that this dispute has no sufficient reason because the Public Works Department's signing of the contract did not bind itself to maintain the rental fee for a certain period of time and not to change it at any time as needed. The owners also claim that the Public Works Department has no right to stipulate the rental fees for the three zones, namely the Public Concession, the French Concession, and the Chinese territory. The French Concession and the Chinese territory are obvious facts, but the discussion refers to rickshaws that solicit business on the roads of the Public Concession, which is also obvious. The representatives of the Rickshaw Owners Guild, who went to the Public Works Department on Tuesday, were informed that the petition submitted by the branch a week ago had been transferred to the relevant authorities and that the guild would be notified of the result within two weeks. The Public Works Department does not want to discuss the petition until it receives the Rickshaw Committee's decision."

Animal Protection Society Requests the Enactment of Animal Cruelty Prevention Regulations 115

In order to promote benevolence and save people's hearts, the China Animal Protection Society has submitted a document to the Legislative Yuan requesting the enactment of articles or regulations prohibiting cruelty to animals in order to supplement the deficiencies of current laws. The original text is as follows: "We respectfully submit this petition. The protection of animals is largely governed by laws in Europe and the United States. These laws have been implemented for a long time and their effectiveness is increasing day by day. Recently, some countries have even included them in their constitutions. Benevolent voices and righteous questions are heard from afar. China was one of the earliest civilizations, and its people have always been known for benevolence and compassion. All things are equal to mankind. There are clear ancient instructions. However, in recent times, people's hearts have become shallow and evil customs have become rampant. Some people satisfy their appetites, while others seek to exploit animals for profit. They use all kinds of cruel methods to inflict pain on defenseless animals, causing injuries everywhere, which is shocking. According to Article 21 of the Detailed Rules for the Implementation of the Hunting Law currently in force in China, 'Local authorities may, depending on local conditions, formulate regulations for the protection of beneficial animals to supplement the Hunting Law and these Detailed Rules.' However, in fact, local authorities have not formulated any regulations for the protection of beneficial animals, so the original intention of the legislation cannot be promoted. When facts occur, officials at all levels use the excuse that there are no laws to rely on and do not prohibit them, or even regard it as far-fetched and laugh at it. This deeply hinders the saving of people's hearts and the elimination of violence. The work of this association is even more difficult to carry out. Therefore, we have extracted and translated one article from the British Hunting Law and one example of animal cruelty, and submitted them to your Yuan. We propose that articles prohibiting cruelty to animals be stipulated in any law, the nature of which should be proactive, or that separate regulations prohibiting cruelty to animals be enacted to supplement the deficiencies of current laws. We humbly await the decision of your Yuan for implementation. This is the great fortune of all living beings."

Municipal Social Affairs Bureau to Hold Spring Plowing Agricultural Loan Preparations Completed and to Begin Immediately 116

In order to solve the economic difficulties of the common people, the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, as a customary practice, must hold an agricultural loan at the beginning of each year's farmers' spring plowing season, so as to facilitate the common people. This year, the sowing season has arrived, and the farmers in various rural areas are in urgent need of funds, so preparations are now actively underway. The loan will be disbursed within one or two weeks at the shortest time. The person in charge of the public loan office in each rural area will issue the loan to the corresponding rural area. In addition, the first public loan office of the bureau on Zhonghua Road, Dananmen, is located in a relatively remote location, making it slightly inconvenient for the poor to borrow. Therefore, from the day before yesterday, it was specially moved to No. 142, Zhaofang Lane, Laoximen, to conduct business.

Representatives of Western Shipping Industry in Pudong Request the Construction of Public Wharves 118

Xing Zhigang, a representative of the western shipping industry in Pudong, submitted a document to the Shanghai Municipal Government yesterday, stating that it was a request to order the Public Works and Engineering Bureaus to relax the shoreline and construct the originally planned Nanhui Guild Hall public wharf to maintain transportation and benefit commerce. It stated that the businesses in the Nanshi area rely heavily on the trading of local ships and fellow villagers. From the Sixteen Pups Wharf to the Dongjiadu Wharf, a distance of three li, there are numerous wharves along the beach. Ships from various regions are assigned specific berths without confusion, which has led to prosperous commerce. This is recorded in the county chronicles and can be verified. Since the shoreline has been taken over by the city, the area from Sixteen Pups southward to Dongjiadu Wharf has been designated as a wharf area. Warehouses have been erected, blocking important passages. The original wharves along the beach have been either destroyed or merged, resulting in limited space. Ships from various regions have nowhere to dock and are scattered. This has led to changes in the Nanshi area, with empty houses lined up, affecting municipal taxes significantly. For example, the previously existing Wanyu, Yongsheng, and Dongjiadu wharves were used by ships from various towns and villages in Shanghai, Fengxian, Nanhui, and Sichuan counties, and commerce was prosperous. Now, after the destruction of the Wanyu and Yongsheng wharves, the Dongjiadu Wharf, which was built by various businesses, has been occupied by the Municipal Finance and Public Works Bureaus. As a result, ships from various villages are scattered, and the market is declining. A portion of the ships have gathered to dock at the Nanhui Guild Hall Wharf. Previously, the Public Works Bureau, together with the Public Utilities Bureau, erected magnetic signs, designating the area as a public wharf. However, the wharf has not yet been constructed, making it difficult for ships from various villages to dock, and the loading and unloading of goods is extremely dangerous. Only those who have personally experienced it can understand the hardship. Therefore, a special request is made to your office to grant permission and review the matter. The wharf is the center of cargo transportation and the lifeline of commerce. It is requested that the Public Works and Engineering Bureaus be ordered to allow the relaxation of the shoreline at the Guild Hall public wharf and to commence construction to facilitate transportation and maintain commerce. The urgency is paramount.

The resolutions are as follows: Selling goods at low prices is self-destructive, especially during this period of rising raw material prices. A warning should be given first, followed by further adjustments. It has been found that one or two businesses are still using old scales, which not only harms fellow businesses but also violates government regulations. If found in the future, the responsible authorities should be asked to handle the matter according to the law. Jiren Coffin Assistance Society Seeks Members to Help Make Coffins 130

The Shanghai Jiren Coffin Assistance Society specializes in providing coffins for the poor who cannot afford them. The society provides a coffin worth 25 yuan, along with charcoal dust, lime, and carrying fees. This service has been provided for 18 years. The operating expenses of the society are covered by the board of directors, and the coffin-making expenses are covered by member contributions. The society does not solicit donations from outside. Mr. Shao Ruxin, the director of the society, plans to expand the services and is seeking new members. The revised bylaws have been drafted, and a meeting of members was held at the Gongdelin Vegetarian Restaurant the night before last to discuss them item by item. The membership will be divided into five groups: Benevolence, Righteousness, Propriety, Wisdom, and Faith, with 500 members in each group. Each coffin requires 500 contributions of 5 cents each, totaling 25 yuan. A charge of 1 yuan per contribution will be levied for every ten coffins. The membership will be capped at 5 groups, after which a general meeting will be held. Until the general meeting is held, the collection of membership fees will be suspended, but coffin assistance will continue as usual. The society will relocate to No. 6 Dakang Lane on the 5th of this month. The proposal was unanimously approved, and the meeting adjourned for dinner until after 9 p.m.

Two Tasks of the Municipal Police Bureau: Relieving Local Vagrants and Inspecting Public Places 131

The Municipal Police Bureau has been actively carrying out tasks such as relieving local vagrants and inspecting public places since January of this year. The work has now concluded, and the results are satisfactory. The details are as follows:

The Municipal Police Bureau has detained and provided relief to a large number of vagrants in the city since January of this year, cooperating with various charitable organizations to send them back to their hometowns. The relief work lasted for three months and ended at the end of last month. Various charitable organizations have been working to send all the vagrants detained by the bureau back to their original homes. This measure has been beneficial to the city's security.

The results are satisfactory. Those operating without complying with the regulations have been strictly dealt with, and those whose fire safety, building layout, and other facilities need to be corrected have been ordered to do so. Li Shaobin, Director of the Municipal North Revenue Office, Found Not Guilty 133

Li Shaobin, director of the Municipal North Revenue Office of the Shanghai Municipal Finance Bureau, was involved in a dispute over the collection of house tax from the Futai Lumber Company in Zhabei. Lu Houfu Injured by a Vehicle 134

Lu Houfu, a 64-year-old man from Tongzhou, lived above the Dongxin Cigarette Shop opposite the small vegetable market at the intersection of Pingliang Road and Manchuria Road. Yesterday afternoon at around 2:00 p.m., Lu was returning home after visiting friends. When he reached the intersection of Manchuria Road and was about to cross the road from east to west, a black-plated car driven by a Westerner was speeding from west to east. Lu Houfu was in the middle of the road, unable to avoid it. The car did not brake or swerve to avoid him and continued to speed straight ahead, causing Lu Houfu to be knocked down and thrown more than ten paces. His left temple and cheekbone were broken, and he bled profusely and fainted on the spot. Fortunately, a police officer from the nearby Yulin Road police station saw the incident and immediately stopped the car, recorded the license plate number, and took the driver to the police station. The injured man was immediately taken to the hospital for treatment. His condition is said to be critical.

Two Suicides 135

Lu Shangzhi Dies from Poisoning. Lu Shangzhi, an employee of the Yuliang Liangxin Pharmacy in Fangbang Street, inside the city, lived at No. 2 Jindeli, Menghua Street, inside the West Gate. His wife indulged in the modern habits of Shanghai, and Lu's salary could not keep up with the high cost of living and the poor economic conditions in Shanghai. Therefore, it was difficult for him to satisfy his wife's demands, and complaints were constant. The day before yesterday, the couple quarreled over money, and his wife angrily cursed him and left, not returning until late at night. In despair, Lu felt that life was worse than death and bought a large amount of opium, which he took to commit suicide. He lay silently in bed. When the landlord did not see Lu leave the house, he became suspicious and went to peek inside. He saw that Lu's face was pale, his breathing was rapid, and his voice was hoarse. Knowing that something was wrong, he immediately notified Lu's friend, who took him to Qu Zhifu Hospital for treatment, but it was to no avail. The hospital reported the incident to the Wenmiao Road Police Station, which ordered the local constable Jiang Pingyang to report it to the District Court for examination.

Cheng Caisheng Drowns Himself. Cheng Caisheng, a 63-year-old man from Suzhou, was alone and had been unemployed for a long time. He had no fixed place to eat or sleep. In the past, he could rely on petty trading to make a living, but now, with all industries in decline, goods were expensive and sales were sluggish, making it difficult to survive. In addition to being burdened with old age and illness, he suffered physically and mentally. He decided to end his life and went to the side of the Lotus Pond of the Yuyuan Garden in the Town God Temple at 8:40 p.m. on March 31 and drowned himself in the river. The park police saw him and immediately rescued him, but he had already swallowed a lot of dirty water, and his lungs and stomach were severely damaged. He was taken to Shanghai Hospital by the police of the Town God Temple, but he died yesterday. The hospital reported the incident to the police station, which ordered the local constable Jiang Pingyang to report it to the District Court for examination. The above two suicide cases were examined by Prosecutor Zhao and Examiners Shen, who ordered that Lu Shangzhi's body be collected by his family and Cheng Caisheng's body be collected by his relatives.

Robbery in Broad Daylight on Xinzha Road 136

At around 11:00 a.m. yesterday, while a family surnamed Mou at No. 4, Lane 221, Datong Road, Xinzha Road, was preparing lunch, three men suddenly entered the house on the pretext of asking for directions. The two bandits then went upstairs to the bedroom and searched the room. In a hurry, they grabbed several expensive clothes from the room and quickly came downstairs. They caught sight of a platinum ring on the hand of the victim, who was being held captive, and forced him to take it off. They then fled out of the house together. After an inspection, the total loss was estimated to be over 250 yuan. The family filed a detailed loss report with the police station and requested an investigation.

Yangtze River Customs Brokers Charter Ships for Cargo Transport 139

Dissatisfied with the Six Companies' Volume Measurement System; Chartering Ning Yong Ji and Other Vessels from Treaty Ports

-- Both Sides Still Attempting to Negotiate a Resolution --

Due to the recent issue of volume measurement along the Yangtze River, customs brokers have revolted, expressing their unacceptability to the Six Companies. Simultaneously, various customs brokers have chartered their own ships, sailing between Shanghai and Hankou, intending to demonstrate their resolute attitude. The Six Companies have been holding meetings for days to discuss this matter, and the situation is quite serious. Details are as follows:

Volume Measurement Issue: Since the Six Companies implemented the public sharing of costs, cargo water transport fees along the Yangtze River have increased, and commissions have decreased. Customs brokers and clients have always had standard size limits for packed goods. For example, a certain type of cargo box would be charged according to a certain number of feet, with a fixed limit. However, clients often privately increased the box area but still paid the original water transport fee. The shipping companies, due to excessive hidden losses, began to implement actual volume measurement for packed goods.

Request for Accommodation: There are dozens of customs brokerages in Shanghai along the Yangtze River. The Six Companies' volume measurement issue has aroused great opposition. Once fees are charged according to measured volume, the customs brokers will be unable to maintain their business. Therefore, a general meeting was convened to resolve this matter through the customs broker's association. Each executive committee member sent a letter to the Six Companies, requesting that the pressure on volume-measured goods not be excessive, and that some leniency be given. For example, a 30-foot box originally made as 12 feet could be changed to 20 feet to show the client's concession. The shipping companies discussed the matter extensively but were unable to accept it.

Each Side Moves to Extremes: The Six Companies have already entrusted foreigners from the Pingzhun Company to implement volume measurement and collect fees based on the actual measured amount. However, clients and customs brokers have become even more opposed. In addition to a large quantity of goods such as metals and sugar being reloaded onto ships of the Xiangtai Foreign Firm, which is not part of the public sharing system, it was originally planned that the customs brokers and clients would jointly form a shipping company to fundamentally avoid loading ships of the Six Companies. Later, due to a lack of dock cargo warehousing and other tools, various customs brokerages chartered merchant vessels such as Yongji, Malai, and Funing, sailing the Yangtze River themselves. They have already started services, determined to sail fully loaded. In addition, with the Six Companies' water transport fee of $12.60 per ton, these several vessels specially reduce the fee to $6 per ton, and can also offer a 10% discount for actual payment.

Final Consultation: Since then, the Six Companies' upstream cargo transportation has inevitably been affected, and future business is feared to be impacted. The Six Companies have convened meetings on this matter repeatedly, already reaching three decisions. Yesterday afternoon, they were discussing this matter again. It is heard that the Six shipping companies can generally express concessions regarding volume-measured goods, calculating the fee at 80%. For example, a 30-foot box can be charged as 24 feet (usually 40 feet is considered one ton). After the agreement is reached, they will contact the customs brokers again, hoping for a peaceful resolution between both sides.

Ming Wah Bank Declared Bankrupt; Creditors' Meeting Held Yesterday 140

Branches in Various Locations Can Hold Creditors' Meetings Locally; Future Distribution of Assets and Liabilities Must Be Centralized in Shanghai

Datong News Agency reports: After the head office of Ming Wah Bank on Beijing Road and the Shanghai, Tianjin, Qingdao Main Branch, North Branch, and Beiping Branch simultaneously closed on May 23rd last year, creditors such as Lu Junfen filed a petition to the First Special District Local Court, requesting a declaration of the bank's bankruptcy. The court accepted the petition and ruled accordingly. Subsequently, in December last year, the First Creditors' Meeting was convened, but due to the failure of branches in various locations to send representatives to Shanghai to attend, auditors and other positions could not be elected. These circumstances were reported in the press. Yesterday afternoon at 3:00 PM, the Second Creditors' Meeting was convened. Details of the situation are as follows:

Creditor Attendance: Yesterday's creditors' meeting was held in the meeting room of the YMCA on Sichuan Road. Attending were 209 creditors, including Wang Jian'e, Le Junfen, Zhou Ziheng, Tang Mao Guan, and Xin Ji, representing a total debt of $187,787.18 (the registered number of creditors in Shanghai was 658, with a total debt of $640,000).

Chairman's Report: Two people, Judge Yu Lude of the First Special Court and bankruptcy administrator accountant An Shao Yun, served as the presidium. Court clerk Ying Yeping served as the recorder. First, Judge Yu reported that the First Creditors' Meeting had no results due to the failure of branches in various locations to send representatives to Shanghai to attend. After careful study by the court, it was decided that Shanghai and the branch offices in various localities could convene creditors' meetings separately on the spot, but that the asset distribution and debt apportionment in the future would have to be centralized in Shanghai.

Election of Auditors: After Judge Yu finished reporting, accountant An Shao Yun reported the number of registered creditors and the amount of debt in Shanghai, as well as the number of attendees and the amount of debt at today's meeting (as seen above). He then discussed the general situation of the bank's liabilities and assets. Finally, discussions began, and creditors' representatives Le Junfen and Wang Jian'e successively expressed their opinions, which can be divided into two points: 1. According to Article 122 of the Bankruptcy Law, the debtor should attend the creditors' meeting. 2. The bank's accounts are unclear, and the creditors all want to file lawsuits. The reason they haven't filed lawsuits is due to a lack of litigation fees. They should request the court to grant litigation assistance according to the provisions of the Civil Code to show sympathy for the creditors. After the chairman answered and the case was recorded and filed, five auditors were elected. After the votes were tallied and counted, Le Junfen, Zhou Ziheng, Tang Mao Guan, Zhou Lun Yuan, and Wang Jian'e were elected. The meeting was then adjourned.

Former Land Bureau Director Jin Liren's Family Undergoes Turmoil 141

His Wife, Lu Canjuan, Sues for Separation; Jin Accuses Lu of Often Staying Out Overnight

Former Shanghai Municipal Land Bureau Director Jin Liren, 30 years ago, was a handsome and unrestrained young man who frequented pleasure quarters. He met the famous courtesan Zhu Xueqing (now Jin's wife, Lu Canjuan). Elegant scholar and beautiful woman, they pledged their love and began living together in the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign of the Qing Dynasty. Their love was single-minded and unwavering for 30 years, living harmoniously, a truly admirable and happy marriage. Unexpectedly, Jin Liren is now 53 years old, and Lu Canjuan is 51 years old. In their twilight years, instead of enjoying the blessings of retirement, they are following the example of young couples today and engaging in divorce litigation. Initially, Lu Canjuan filed a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court, seeking a divorce from Jin Liren, citing that Jin had another lover. However, the case was rejected for lack of jurisdiction. Lu Canjuan then hired lawyer Ling Qihong to file a complaint with the Nanshi Local Court, changing the request to separation and requesting a lump-sum payment of $30,000 in alimony. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Han Jingdou of the Local Court opened a mediation hearing. Jin Liren and Lu Canjuan did not attend; their agent lawyer Ling represented them in court. Regarding the reasons for requesting mediation, it was stated that they married in the 32nd year of the Guangxu reign, with a matchmaker. For more than 30 years, their relationship was harmonious. Recently, Jin's financial situation improved, while she aged and lost her beauty. Therefore, he secretly took a Cantonese woman named Mai as a concubine. To the woman who suffered with him, she was nothing more than a thorn in his eye, suffering unbearable abuse. Therefore, she requested separation and requested an order for a lump-sum payment of $30,000 in alimony. Jin Liren, accompanied by his hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Wu Baotai, stated in court that his first wife had passed away long ago, and Lu Canjuan was originally Zhu Xueqing from a Shanghai brothel. They had lived together for 30 years, and their relationship was generally good. Until a few years ago, Lu suddenly changed her behavior, often staying out overnight, taking away valuable clothing, jewelry, antiques, etc. She falsely claimed to go to Hangzhou with her cousin Zhou Shuan for business. She suddenly filed for divorce in the First Special Court, but the case was rejected due to jurisdictional issues. Now, she is falsely requesting separation in this case. I have lived with her for 30 years and have never heard of this relative named Zhou. Moreover, it has been found that Zhou is Feng Zimei, alias Hedongsheng, from the record of singing fruit rewards. Outside rumors slander me as a cuckold. After decades of marriage, she changed her mind when she already knew her fate, leading to an unfortunate event. My reputation has been completely ruined, and I am extremely heartbroken. I have already pursued the matter with the Special Court. As for her not being my legal wife, she is not legally bound and is free to leave in her later years. The court determined that mediation could not be established and ordered her to file a formal lawsuit.

Ship Has an Exhibition Hall; Public Viewing Today

The World Liner Reliance of the Hengbao Company on Guangdong Road in the port arrived in Shanghai last night, carrying a world tour group of 232 people. Details are as follows:

Group Members Arrive in Shanghai: The World Liner, especially the Reliance of Hengbao Company, is visiting Shanghai for the first time. The ship departed from New York, carrying a total of 232 world tour group members. It first passed through Europe and then through the South Seas Islands to Shanghai. The ship entered the port last night, but the group members did not go ashore that night, so it was changed to 8:00 AM this morning, docking at the Gonghexiang Wharf.

Touring the City: The Shanghai Hengbao Company has pre-planned the tour itinerary for each group member upon their arrival in Shanghai. When they disembarked at 8:00 AM in the morning, they immediately boarded 70 Xiang Sheng cars, hired to visit Wusong, Jiangwan, Zhabei, Longhua, and other places. At noon, they will rest and have lunch at the Race Course Hotel. In the afternoon, they are scheduled to tour the British and French Concessions by rickshaw, but since the rickshaw pullers are on strike, they may switch to cars.

Heading North Tomorrow Morning: Each person will stay in Shanghai for one day and return to the ship that night. The ship will leave Shanghai tomorrow morning and head to Qinhuangdao. The group members will go to Beijing, Tianjin, and other places for sightseeing, and some will go to the Great Wall. Then, they will take the original ship to Japan, cross the Pacific Ocean, pass through Honolulu and San Francisco, and then return to New York via the Panama Canal. On the 9th of this month, there will be a third group of more than 400 people on the Franco-Weihao ship arriving in Shanghai.

Reception and Viewing: This time, on the German ship Reliance, an exhibition hall is set up on the highest floor, displaying German art products, music supplies, and crafts, divided into porcelain, clay, and machine-made products, personal items, and new-era furniture and garden utensils, and new-style sports equipment, etc. Therefore, Hengbao Company has specially invited Chinese and Western people from all walks of life in Shanghai to visit the ship. The purpose of its exhibits is not for sale, but for exhibition, to let people from all over the world know about the products of the new Germany and arouse a new kind of contact. The reception time is from 10:00 AM to 12:00 PM today.

Xu Qizhong's Extravagance and Debauchery Reach Extremes; Banquets Cost Over a Thousand Dollars, and a Night of Dancing Reaches a Hundred Dollars; Car Horns with Nine Different Sounds, Extravagant Actions Too Numerous to List 143

--Creditors Oppose Bankruptcy, Seeking Punishment for Squandering--

Xu Qizhong, the son of wealthy merchant Xu Guannan, is only 22 years old. He is a typical纨绔子弟 (spoiled rich kid) who excels in eating, drinking, whoring, and gambling. Relying on his parents' indulgence, he does not engage in production but treats gold like dirt. When his spending runs out and he can no longer conjure wealth, he borrows from all directions. Cunning people, knowing that he is the son of a wealthy family, are happy to lend to him, but expect him to repay several times the amount in the future. For example, last winter, Wang Pingzhong (i.e., Wang Bingzong, Wang Pingjia, Wang Xinchu) attempted to swindle tens of thousands of dollars from Xu but failed. He instead accused Xu of

Forging a Bill: The First Special District Local Court held a clear trial and found Xu innocent. Meanwhile, the prosecutor investigated the reasons for Wang's false accusation and filed a public prosecution against Wang. Currently, Wang has escaped without a trace, so the case has not yet been opened for trial. However, Xu knows that there are many loan receipts where he borrowed one thousand and repaid ten thousand. The debts from eating, drinking, whoring, and gambling are even greater. Since it is difficult to ask his parents to repay them on his behalf, and there is no platform to escape debt, he submitted a petition to the First Special Court,

Requesting Bankruptcy: The court has already convened a creditors' meeting for him, but it has not been successful. Now, the auditor hired by the creditors, lawyer Le Junwei, has thoroughly reviewed his debts, and most are due to squandering. If he is allowed to declare bankruptcy, it will not only cause great losses to legitimate creditors but also encourage extravagance and debauchery. Therefore, creditors such as Sincere Company, Syntong Motor Car Company, Shih Ho Jewelry Company, Jinlong Hotel, and the woman Hu Meiying, jointly hired lawyer Le Junwei to file a

Criminal Private Prosecution: Briefly stated, Xu is the only son of Xu Guannan, a wealthy merchant from Wuxing. Although young, he does not know about farming. He creates a den of consumption on the sea, indulging in sensual pleasures and extravagant entertainment. He enjoys everything that exhausts the luxury of food and clothing, reaching the peak of debauchery. Therefore, dinners at the Atlantic cost over a thousand dollars, and a night of dancing at the Paramount costs a hundred dollars. Other examples include keeping beauties in golden houses and seeking new-style furniture. Spending a thousand dollars on smiles requires fashionable clothing. Therefore, Hongxiang Company,

Gaohe Women's Shoes: Store, Shih Ho Jewelry Store, Zou Juxing Clothing Store, Yiyuan Furniture Company, Jinlong Hotel, Sincere Company, St. Anna Dance Hall, Daxia Motor Car Company, etc., are owed hundreds to more than two thousand dollars. His own car has nine different horns and is equipped with a long and short-wave wireless radio. All these decorations are unique in Shanghai. Other extravagant actions are too numerous to list. There is also the owner of the Wendi Brothel, Zheng Huizhen, to whom the defendant once owed a common hall fee of one thousand dollars. Because he had no funds to repay, he gave her a loan receipt for 10,000 yuan. This shows that the defendant is willing to squander, truly

An Innovation of Spoil Rich Son: It is a bad example for young people and a parasite on society. He is using his intelligence and deceit, falsely declaring bankruptcy, hoping to evade debt and damage creditor rights. He has already constituted the crime stipulated in Article 154, paragraph 1, of the Bankruptcy Law, detrimental to the rights of creditors, and Article 156, paragraph 1, of squandering. According to the statement, the court has already issued a summons to the defendant to appear in court this Saturday afternoon to await investigation.

Continued Trial on the 4th of This Month

Fan Qiu, the daughter-in-law of Fan Huichun (i.e., the daughter of wealthy paint merchant Qiu Weiqing), accused her husband, Fan Chunsheng, of adultery in the French Concession Police Station. They were caught red-handed and handed over to the Second Special District Court. Because neither party attended, the lawyers representing Fan Qiu, Zhang Deqin, and Fan Chunsheng, Wu Baodi, agreed to postpone the hearing. This has been reported in the press. It is now learned that although the relatives of both parties have tried their best to mediate, and according to those familiar with the Fan family's situation, the name of the protagonist of the adultery case is Little Diamond, that is, Fan's favorite concubine, a girl from Guilin known as Oil Bottle. At home, she addresses Chunsheng as brother and sister. Years ago, she was once engaged to the son of rice merchant Gu, but the marriage did not happen. Since her relationship with Chunsheng, Qiu has been suspicious. However, the father-in-law saw through the hidden situation and, for the sake of consolidating the family reputation and succession, ordered his son to go to Dongying (Japan) with his daughter-in-law to study, hoping to cut off the love affair in one fell swoop, achieving two goals at once. Who knew that Qiu was not accustomed to living abroad, and Chunsheng did not dare to disobey his father's orders by going alone. After a few months, they returned to Shanghai. There were many obstacles at home, and they persuaded Little Diamond to obtain her mother's consent to rent a small building on Rue Sainte Marie, where they lived together. Chunsheng only sees his wife Qiu every few days, and marital pleasure is like a nominal affair. However, Qiu still believed that her father-in-law still had some regard for her. Recently, because her father-in-law changed his attitude and stood on the same line as his son, he suddenly ordered his daughter-in-law Qiu to move out and live separately. Qiu was extremely angry, and soon, the act of catching adultery was plotted. It is now heard that the case has been scheduled for a continued trial on the 4th of this month. Qiu's relatives are afraid that there will be many spectators, and it is heard that they have entrusted someone to pre-distribute spectator tickets to avoid missing the opportunity.

His accomplice, Cao Ziqing (25 years old, from Haimen), lives at No. 2 Longxing Lane, Route Contaut. They were ordered to be detained, pending investigation and delivery to the court for interrogation. Wine Enters Sad Bowels, Difficult to Dissipate Resentment; Heartbroken Traveler Commits Suicide 147

Neck Cut Once, Esophagus Fortunately Not Severed

Chen Longgen, 43 years old, from Nantong, used to live in Sanyi Township, his hometown, and worked as a farmer. He had a small amount of savings and his family was considered to be moderately wealthy. Last winter, the township was suddenly washed by a large group of bandits. Chen's house was burned down, and his wife and children were shot dead. Chen felt the tragedy of his family's destruction and suffered a great mental shock. He would sometimes cry and sometimes laugh. After medical treatment, the illness began to improve slightly. Chen came to Shanghai to seek work, but without success. Yesterday afternoon at 4:38 PM, Chen went to the Jiucai Restaurant opened by Wu Lianhui, a native of Chongming, at No. 50, Laozhen Street, Hongzhen, Zhabei. He called for wine and dishes and drank alone. Wine entered his sad bowels, and resentment was difficult to dissipate. He suddenly conceived the idea of ending his life, pushed away the cup, quietly took a knife for cutting vegetables from the restaurant, aimed it at his neck, and slashed hard. The restaurant owner, Wu Lianhui, caught a glimpse of it and stepped forward to grab the knife. Chen was already injured and collapsed, bleeding profusely. Wu reported the situation to the Hongzhen Police Station and summoned an ambulance. Police officer Zhao Yushu rushed Chen to Tongren Hospital for treatment. It is said that the injury was not light, but fortunately, the esophagus was not severed and his life was not in danger.

Shanghai's Woolen Industry (3) 162

— Edited by China Zheng

(Shanghai Industrial and Commercial Overview No. 20)

3. The Woolen Manufacturing Industry in this Port

As mentioned earlier, the woolen fabrics sold in our country are still dominated by imported goods. Therefore, there are not many people engaged in manufacturing in this port, and the scale is small. Now, only Zhanghua and China Weiyi, two relatively large companies, will be introduced later. In addition, if there are three companies, Huadong, Tianxiang, and Hongfa, that specialize in making camel hair, they will be attached together because of their large scale and relevance to this article, for the reference of those who are enthusiastic about the national goods movement:

1. Zhanghua Wool Spinning and Weaving Company - The factory was established in October of the 18th year of the Republic of China. Capital of 800,000 yuan. A general factory was established in Zhoujiadu, Pudong, Shanghai, and a branch factory was established in Tianjin. It was founded by Liu Hongsheng, the former general manager of the China Merchants Bureau. Mr. Liu currently serves as chairman and general manager. There are currently 70 weaving machines and 2,200 wool spinning machines, some of which are old machines from the former Rihui Port No. 1 Wool Weaving Factory, and some were ordered from Belgium. There are currently 6700 workers, and most of the raw materials are sourced from within China. The products are mostly thin serge, military uniform fleece, and patterned fleece, which are sold in this port and throughout the country. The annual turnover reaches more than 2 million yuan.

2. China Weiyi Wool Spinning and Weaving Factory - The factory was established in the 8th year of the Republic of China. It was initially opened by Mr. Li Ansu with his own investment. In the 13th year of the Republic of China, foreign shares were added and it was reorganized into a limited company. It was reorganized again in the 17th year, stipulating a capital of 60,000 taels of silver, and the organization was changed to unlimited. Ju Tang, the son of shareholder Xu Linfu, serves as the manager. The factory site is located at No. 170, Xiaoshadu Road. There are 16 machines of various sizes in the factory, with a total of 160 employees. In the 23rd year of the Republic of China, it acquired the Danan Camel Hair Factory on Radu Road and expanded its scope. Its products are divided into three types: woolen fabrics, woolen yarn, and camel hair. Branch offices have been established in Suzhou and Hangzhou, and there are several managers in Beiping and Beijing to promote sales.

3. Huadong Wool Weaving and Camel Hair Factory - The factory is a partnership organization established in January of the 20th year of the Republic of China with a capital of 50,000 yuan. The shareholders include Chen Youyun and Zhang Zhongliang, with Chen Jun concurrently serving as the manager. The factory is located at No. 156, Alabaster Road, with eight weaving machines, one fleece machine, and one hundred male and female workers and fifteen or sixteen employees. Specializing in weaving various camel hair.

4. Tianxiang Camel Hair Weaving Factory - The factory was established in the 17th year of the Republic of China with a capital of 50,000 yuan, which was increased to 100,000 yuan in the 20th year. It is a joint-stock company, with Shen Dehua, Rong Tingquan, etc. as directors, Shen Zhuming, Lin Ruiting, etc. as supervisors, and Fan Lianqin as manager. The manufacturing department is located at No. 343, Xujiahui Road, and the business department is located at No. 48, Jingyuan Street, Guangdong Road. There are twelve camel hair machines and more than 180 male and female workers, which can produce more than 30 camel hair codes per year. Because there are no suitable wool threads in China, most of the raw materials are purchased from abroad and ordered by various foreign firms in this port. The main sales areas are this port and the Yangtze River basin.

5. Hongfa Woolen Weaving Factory - The factory is located at No. 1741 and a half, Labor Shen Road, with a capital of 100,000 yuan. It was initially operated as a partnership by Li Changzuo, Wu Pinrui, etc. It was reorganized in June of the 23rd year of the Republic of China and operated solely by Wu Pinrui. Later, Mr. Li Yunxun joined the cooperation, so its organization is still a partnership. Mr. Li is currently the manager. There are ten machines and a set of steel wire machines in the factory, employing about one hundred workers. It can produce about one thousand yards of camel hair per day. It is said that the raw materials are waste hair and self-made wool yarn.

It was recently heard that the Japanese businessman Yoshida Yoko is planning to establish a woolen weaving factory in Shanghai, specializing in weaving wool and other woolen fabrics, and selling them in various parts of our country. It is said that it is currently in preparation.

A Total of Twelve Matches from May 19 to June 9; Seven Players from this Port and North China Went to Hong Kong Yesterday for Preliminary Selection

The soccer team from our country that will attend the 11th World Games to be held in Berlin this August has had thirty candidates selected by the National Sports Association. From Preliminary Selection to Departure

For the preliminary selection, the National Sports Association specially sent Rong Qizhao as a representative to Hong Kong in advance to preside over everything. The preliminary selection will be held from the 4th to the 10th, and the thirty candidates will take turns to play in the matches, and then select the official representatives. The team will then continue to practice in Hong Kong. The scheduled order is: 18th against Hong Kong Military United, 19th against the Mixed Team, and the 24th the whole team will arrive in Shanghai from Hong Kong. It is scheduled to play another match in Shanghai. The date has been set for the 25th, 26th, and 29th. The original date for departure was May 7th, but because the contract with Java was set for the 15th, the team could not depart early. The team was then rescheduled to depart from Shanghai on May 2nd on the French mail ship Jean Laborp, which will detour to Saigon before heading to the South Seas. The team is required to arrive in Dutch Java by May 15th, and then transfer to Singapore, Penang, Siam, Yangon, Calcutta, and then to Germany. The team will compete with local strong teams in each port along the way to gain practice. As for the track and field, basketball, swimming, boxing, weightlifting and other athletes and staff who will attend the World Games, they are scheduled to depart around June 20th.

Education News

Amidst Calls for Developing the Northwest, Shanxi Education Makes Rapid Progress 174

Increase budget allocations to expand new endeavors, rectify local education to strengthen secondary education, implement specialized education, and conduct civic training.

In recent years, all construction undertakings in Shaanxi have seen rapid progress. In terms of education, the expansion and improvement of quantity and quality are no longer what they used to be. In the area of school education, Shaanxi was in a state of stagnation due to the continuous disasters of the 18th and 19th years of the Republic of China. Since Zhou Xuechang took charge of the Department of Education, he has tried to restore existing facilities and formulate a plan to gradually increase the budget allocation to seek the development of emerging industries. Therefore, in recent years, elementary schools have shown considerable achievements. The province, feeling the unevenness of elementary school teachers, established an elementary school teacher training institute to select teachers from various counties for short-term training, improve their teaching methods, and increase their knowledge so that they can continue to improve and not be outdated. Furthermore, the institute has also set up classes for administrative personnel and social education personnel to strive for the improvement of local educational administration and the advancement of social education. In the past one or two years, the students of the institute have been assigned to various counties and have been able to make special efforts. As for the annual summer seminars held in various districts, strict examination of elementary school textbooks, compilation of local supplementary reading materials by county, and the implementation of district inspections are all necessary measures for the promotion of elementary education. In the province's secondary education, middle schools focus on the cultivation of national culture, normal schools focus on professional training, and vocational schools are numerous. Last year, with the increase in provincial funding, the Provincial Department of Education purchased a large number of instruments worth nearly 100,000 yuan based on the current situation of each school, distributed them to the schools to enrich equipment, registered teachers, formulated specific standards for various courses and teaching progress, reviewed textbooks for various subjects to improve teaching, promulgated implementation plans for moral education in secondary normal schools and vocational schools, compiled brief biographies of local worthies, held scientific lectures, and implemented strict management to rectify the academic atmosphere, gradually promoting its effectiveness. Recently, due to the disturbances caused by the Red Bandits in northern Shaanxi, the youth have been anesthetized by them and their minds are chaotic. It is necessary to implement specialized education in Yulin Middle School and Suide Normal School. In the original curriculum, specialized education materials will be added by subject, in order to bring students' thoughts and actions into the right track, so that they can set an example and serve as teachers for Sun Yat-sen's civil schools in the future. This kind of facility is extremely important, and the provincial government has passed its methods and rules and issued them for implementation. The department plans to extend specialized education to the northern and southern regions in the next year in order to expand its scope and lay the foundation for the Three Principles of the People education. As for social education, the province has recently conducted civic training very actively. The provincial capital stipulates that each household must select an adult between the ages of 25 and 50 for training. The training period is set at three months, with half a day of training every Sunday. The subjects include civic knowledge, civic songs, strict training, and spiritual lectures. The implementing agencies are the Provincial Department of Education, the Provincial Government's Pacification Commissioner's Office, the Northwest Political Training Office, the Provincial Party Headquarters, and the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau, which jointly form the Provincial Capital Civic Training Committee to promote it. All citizens' training is conducted in a completely compulsory education manner. The first phase has started with 32 sessions and 50 classes. Since its implementation, the results have been remarkable. This type of facility is a pioneering effort in the Northwest, and is also an emerging undertaking in the country. The Provincial Department of Education plans to complete the provincial civic training within one year and then promote its implementation in other counties. The provinces in the Northwest have heard of this and are sending personnel to the province to observe and imitate it.
