Tomorrow is Children's Day, Celebrations in All Circles of the City 180

Celebration ceremony to be held at the Municipal Stadium at 9 AM, with airplane, fire, national arts, and machine gun performances. The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs has formulated measures for labor children to participate.

April 4th is Children's Day. This year also happens to be the nationally designated Children's Year. The central government has issued an order to all regions to hold enlarged celebrations on this day. The city's party and government agencies and organizations have jointly formed a preparatory committee to prepare for the enlarged celebrations, and the preparations have been completed. The celebration ceremony will be held at the Municipal Stadium at 9 AM tomorrow, with performances and entertainment. The Shanghai Social News reporter has compiled the following information:

Scheduled Order of Celebration Ceremony

The celebration ceremony will be held at the Municipal Stadium in the central district at 9 AM on the 4th. The order is as follows: Perform the ceremony as required, Preparatory Committee report, Mayor Wu's address, Addresses by representatives of party and government agencies, Speeches, Response by children's representatives, Performances, Gifts, Ceremony concludes. The members of the presidium are Mayor Wu Tiecheng, Director of the Bureau of Social Affairs Wu Xingya, Director of the Bureau of Education Pan Gongzhan, Director of the Bureau of Health Li Ting'an, Director of the Bureau of Public Security Cai Jinjun, Director of the Bureau of Public Utilities Xu Peihuang, Garrison Commander Yang Hu, and representatives from the Municipal Party Department Children's Welfare Association, Children's Year Implementation Association, and China Children's Welfare Association, a total of 11 people.

Wonderful Performance Programs

After the ceremony, various programs will be performed, all of which are wonderful, including: Aviation School airplane performance, Municipal Security Team machine gun performance, Municipal Public Security Bureau fire performance, Municipal Orchard Management National Arts performance, China vs. South China football performance, He'an Elementary School Boy Scouts and National Arts performance. All will be held in the Municipal Stadium until 4 PM. In addition, on this day, all movie theaters will show children's movies at 10 AM, providing free admission for children to watch.

Measures for Labor Children to Participate

The Municipal Bureau of Social Affairs issued a special order yesterday to factories to select apprentices and child laborers to participate, and to labor children schools to select workers' children to participate. The measures are as follows: The number of labor children participating from each factory and school shall be determined by the factory and school themselves, the more the better. Each factory and school must designate one representative from the participating labor children to be selected as a citywide labor children representative, to meet with the mayor and speak at the conference. Each factory and school must also appoint several staff members to take care of the labor children participating from their factory and school. All factories must arrive at the Municipal Central District, Guohua Road Stadium command platform before 8:30 AM on the morning of the 4th, and the leader shall report to the labor children registration office. The registration items are as follows: (A) Name of the participating factory or labor children school, (B) Name of the care staff, (C) Name of the children's representative, (D) Number of participating children. After registration, the meeting will send personnel to lead the entry. All participating children must wear clean and tidy clothes. All participating factories and schools must prepare a white cloth flag (3 Chinese feet long and 1 Chinese foot wide) with the words "Labor Children of a Certain Factory or Labor Children School" written on it. The round-trip transportation costs for the labor children must be borne by each participating factory and school, and refreshments will be provided by the meeting.

Transportation Costs for Needy Children Will Be Provided

Regarding homeless needy children, the association has sent letters to various charity orphanages and other welfare institutions in the city, such as the Zhabei Children's Welfare Group, Longhua Orphanage, Vagrant Work Training Center, People's Education Center, and Children's Welfare Institute, to send children in their care to participate on this day. The vehicles will be provided by the institutions, and the transportation costs will be paid by the association.

Fourteen Radio Stations Broadcast Speeches

The association has contacted fourteen broadcasting stations, including Zhongxi, Buddhist, Gospel, Great China, Huamei, Mainland, Li Shutang, Xin Xin, Guohua, Zhongyan, and Municipal Government, to broadcast programs related to children on this day, and has invited Mayor Wu, Secretary-General Yu, Director Wu, Director Pan, Director Li, Director Xu, Director Cai, Tong Xingbai, Jiang Huaishu, Wu Kaixian, Zhang Binghui, Hu Shuyi, and the Chinese Anti-Tuberculosis Association to give speeches.

Special Celebration Issue Has Been Compiled

Major Manufacturers Generously Donate Gifts

Commercial News

Finance, Major Players Buy in on Dips, Gold Standard Remains Steady 183

Yesterday's gold market saw stability as major players bought in on the dips after signs of a downtrend. There were some momentary hesitations, but the buying pressure from major players prevailed, leading to continued steadiness in the end. Early in the morning, news from overseas silver markets indicated that London was long flat and the US was even. There were rumors that some Indian buyers were actually buying at the listed price after the close, and the Montri forward silver price was unchanged or up a fraction of a cent. Exchange rates continued to rise, London gold was unchanged, and the Central Bank's listing revealed that both British and American currencies were even, and the customs gold unit was unchanged. The standard gold price was still listed at 1143.9 yuan. Outside the market, preparatory transactions opened at around 45 yuan. Dadechen and others bought bars, rising to 5.67 yuan. Futaiyong, Dafa Yong, and others supplied at high prices, retreating to 5.34 yuan. The morning opening was slightly higher, and then fell slightly, but gradually recovered as major players bought in on the dips. However, the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's listing revealed that the British was flat and the US was up 0.0625, causing a slight struggle, but buyers were actively moving at high prices, making it difficult to rise. Soon after, it fell slightly again. The silver equalization tax was revealed to be up half a cent. After that, the overall situation stabilized and lacked change. In the afternoon market, it was stable and then slightly weak, with little trading volume. Later, major players suddenly came together to buy bars, gradually turning firm in the end. The April-May spread was posted by the longs at 5.1 yuan. The day's market conditions are recorded below:

The morning opening was 1145.4 yuan, up 0.4 yuan from the previous close. Futaiyong Qianyuanyong sold off, encountering 5.1 yuan. Fuxingyong, Dadechen, Xianghe Huidexiang, Yuanmaoyong, Tianchengxiang, and others took in bars, rising to 5.9 yuan. Yicheng and Dadechen sold off, and the Hongkong and Shanghai Banking Corporation's listing revealed that the British was flat and the US was up 0.0625, reaching 5.7 yuan. Wenfengh Hengding Kang, Tongyurong, Xianghe bought bars, rising to 6.4 yuan. Dingkang, Fuxingyong, Yongde Huidexiang, and Dafa Yong sold off, encountering 5.6 yuan. The silver equalization tax was revealed to be up half a cent, and the situation stabilized. Tianchengxiang and Dadechen slightly took in, rising to 5.9 yuan. Shengyuanyong and Fuxingyong sold slightly, and were even flatter. The noon close was 1145.8 yuan.

The afternoon market opened at 1145.8 yuan. Yuanmaoyong and Tong Hengzhifa Yong sold off, trading around 5.6 yuan. Daheng, Fuxingyong, Dadechen, Yurongxinxiang jointly bought bars, rising to 6.4 yuan. Huidexiang and Qiafenyong sold off, retreating to 6 yuan. Fuxingyong Dafa Yong and Hengchangyong all entered, and the close was 1146.4 yuan. After the close, it was flat.

Shen Bao Literary Weekly

Soul Suicide 203

— Fei Er

On the second afternoon of my arrival in Penang, I found an old friend, Zhang Hui, at a Chinese newspaper office. The first thing he said to me was:

"Hu Wenbo, a teacher in Bukit Mertajam, is dead!"

"What happened?"

"He was crushed to death by real life!" he said coldly. "Tomorrow, you should go to the funeral too! I'm done with my work now and I'm going to the widow's house. You'll know everything tomorrow."

I walked aimlessly down the grey streets of Penang. Over the years, the shadows of young friends had disappeared one by one around me; my heart was filled with sadness and fear.

〇〇 died; Hu Wenbo also died! The weak died; the brave also died. The world is one, yet the ways people die are ever-changing. Death begets the future; yet it also buries the past. How did our Hu Wenbo die?"

I spent the entire afternoon thinking about this. I tried my best to search my memory for stories. I thought about how Hu Wenbo had graduated from a university in northern China, how he had rolled around in the waves of southern China; and how he had deserted, burying his youthful vitality in the southern wilderness; and now, Hu Wenbo was dead! Did he kill himself, or did society kill him?

Let the facts show me!

The next morning at eight o'clock, I went to the pier. A crowd was stirring on the pier. There were reporters from the Chinese newspaper, teachers from Chinese schools, fellow townsmen "towkays," and young students.

A small motorboat was sailing over from the other side. The placid strait was churning up spray. The strait sparkled with gold in the bright sun, while the sorrowful crowd wore grey faces in the scorching sun.

As the motorboat reached the shore, mournful music began to play. The procession was immersed in silent grief, and the leaves on the shore rustled in the breeze.

A black coffin was carried ashore by workers. Behind it, a young widow wearing mourning clothes wept with her head bowed, and two children aged six or seven tugged at their mother's skirt, crying along with her.

Then 〇〇〇 came out of the motorboat. He waved his hand, directing the procession forward.

At the very front was a banner with black characters written on white cloth: "Sending Mr. Hu Wenbo's Soul to Rest." Next was a hired Indian band. Following was the coffin. Then the deceased's young wife, and two young children. Closely following was a team of children wearing white uniforms, divided into three large cars. Finally, were the deceased's fellow townsmen, and friends attending the funeral.

I was sandwiched in the middle of the procession. The heat was steaming my brain. The procession passed by in silence. Only the sound of the cars running over the street, and the weeping of the widow and orphans, occasionally carried by the breeze. The Indian band was listlessly playing mournful music lacking rhythm, and the grey forests of Penang Island occasionally flew past the corner of our eyes.

Close behind the deceased and the widow's carriage, the hooves of the horses in our carriage also rang out on the street, more suited than the Indian music to express the rhythms of human grief.

Wei Jiang sat on my left. At first, he remained silent, but once the conversation started, words flowed smoothly under his calm face:

"Hu Wenbo, a cowardly bug! A useless intellectual. Fire flashed before his eyes, and he jumped up; darkness fell before his eyes, and he retreated. He had knowledge and passion, but lacked will. You see him jumping here and there, embracing the so-called 'conscience' and running around, but in the end, the intellectual's conscience died along with his body and passion!

"He retreated from the motherland, dragging his wife, and eventually his children, serving as a teacher, a reporter, a translator for mines and rubber plantations, and also as a clerk in companies. Oppressed by life, he abandoned his career as a teacher and reporter to become a translator or clerk for big 'towkays', but when his 'conscience' couldn't stand the blatant facts before him, he returned to being a primary school teacher. He traveled between British and Dutch possessions, hitting a wall everywhere for himself or for others, and finally his strong body was worn down, and his soul was wounded."

Wei Jiang paused for a moment, adding:

"Ah, what a clean soul!"

Then he said:

"Friends couldn't bear to see him like that, and often encouraged him:

"'Ah, Wenbo, lift up your head! Turn your eyes to the sun!'

"But it was no use. His head drooped even lower, and his eyes became gloomy and suppressed. He said:

"'I feel like I'm old! I'm already useless!'

"I said:

"'Hu Wenbo is already dead! He is beyond salvation!'

"What do you think he said? He admitted:

"'Yes. I'm dead! I think I've already turned into a grey animal; and this grey animal is about to perish!'

"Sure enough, after that, he blamed himself and cursed himself every day, hoping to end his life quickly. He became despondent, and he destroyed himself in various ways. His purpose has been achieved today."

Wei Jiang's words gradually became agitated, but he restrained himself, and he calmly continued the story:

"Finally, he got sick. He coughed up mouthfuls of blood. Ruo Ping (today's widow) advised him to go to the hospital. He said:

"'What money do I have to go to the hospital?'

"But when death came before his eyes, he was afraid of dying again. So, the fellow townsmen 'towkays' sent him to the hospital. They said:

"'It's so pitiful, this young man.'

"So I admit that he committed suicide, and 〇〇〇〇 〇〇."

As the procession stopped, the sun did not shine on the dead in the overseas Chinese cemetery.

A tomb had already been dug, and after the coffin was lowered, a pile of flowers ended the fate of a certain type of intellectual in this century. The widow's wailing could not call back the grief of the soul, and the condolences of friends could not save the life of a coward.

The procession on the way back seemed more lively: the living rejoiced that they had not yet perished; the "towkays" praised the dead; the widow and orphans cried about the gloomy future; some of the young students wiped their noses and tears, while others were lively and immediately laughing. The Indian band was scattered like defeated soldiers, and the streets of Penang still seemed coldly lifeless under the hot sun. But Zhang Jiang said angrily:

"Soul suicide is an unforgivable sin in this century. The meaning of our funeral is only to bury the past, not to enlighten the future."

The next day, in the HuaWen newspaper obituary that Wei Jiang edited, the subtitle of his memorial article was:

"Helping orphans is welcoming the future era; mourning the dead is sending away the decaying present!"

Then I understood the meaning of Wei Jiang's cold face, even though his article had aroused some antipathy among the overseas Chinese friends.

Preface to "Common Collection" 204

— Mu Mutian

This small collection contains some essays I wrote during the so-called "Year of Essayettes." With very few exceptions, they were written from the autumn of 1933 to the summer of 1934. Because of the popularity of literary supplements, essayettes naturally flourished. Although I had never intended to write this type of thing amidst this uniquely Chinese phenomenon, I somehow followed the trend and wrote some short articles of this nature.

Writing month after month, I never really counted how many I had written; I kept the manuscripts, but I never thought about publishing them as a collection. Although some people asked me if I wanted to publish these short articles, firstly, the quantity was small, and secondly, I always felt that these essays were more trouble than they were worth. Therefore, the result was always a refusal.

Originally, these things were destined to disappear. However, they followed me on my travels, to "summer resorts," to "villas," and then, in my luggage, they came back with me, and they became the beloved infants I cherished. I treasured them, and then I felt that they were my past life.

Friends advised me to collect them, so I selected some, discarded a portion, and compiled about seven or eight tenths of the total quantity into this collection. As a result, the quantity was surprisingly large, and I myself was surprised.

After the compilation was completed, the problem of naming it arose. After several days of work, I finally settled on the two characters "Common" (平凡). Because the two characters "Common" suited my state of mind at the time and were most representative of the characteristics of these miscellaneous essays, I named it "Common Collection" (平凡集). When I mentioned the word "Collection" (集), I always felt like it sounded old-fashioned. But, just using the two characters "Common" (平凡) felt a bit insufficient, and so, I compromised.

Over the years, my state of mind has gradually become common. It is not surprising that a child born of the earth wants to align their life with the pace of the earth. Demons do not fall from angels, but are sons of the earth, and I have thought this way every year. On my long journey through life, I once longed for the distant horizon, where human habitation ends. However, this past feeling is now a cloud of smoke in my memory. Because, I am becoming more common day by day, I love the mundane world, I love the commonness of humanity. The sons of the earth must be in step with the earth's commonness.

Living on the earth, every day should be spent working: whether it is going to battle, building bridges, or paving roads, anything is fine, as long as it benefits the people on earth. Perhaps the miscellaneous essays in "Common Collection" were written with a little bit of a patching-up purpose. However, they are common and not extraordinary. In this kind of common work, I have offended people, but I have also met some new friends. "Chopping is not as round as shaving" (砍的不如削的圓). Those who like to pick on you will always have their say. These miscellaneous essays are some patching-up work. Naturally, one cannot start from ABC, provide a lengthy introduction, and omissions and grammatical errors are inevitable. Misunderstandings are common; but, assuming that those who attacked me in the past did not have ulterior motives, let their attacks become "past." Unmalicious attacks should be forgotten.

However, on the other hand, during that year of writing these miscellaneous essays, I also met some new friends; one of them is unforgettable, and that is Mr. Chen Junzhi. But that young man from Yangzhou died of a terrible disease, and he died in a foreign land! Ever since becoming friends after a decisive debate, he often advised me to write more miscellaneous essays and later collect them into a collection, adding the texts of those who opposed me in the debate: I have always remembered this advice. There was once a debate about movies, but because that was not my own field, I didn't even want my own articles, let alone include the other party's articles. However, the debate with Junzhi was handled according to Junzhi's wishes. Whether I was right in the debate itself and whether there was a conclusion is another matter. However, what is expressed here is not hostility, but rather a kind of friendship.

This collection is not poetry, but essays. However, it reveals my emotions everywhere. Naturally, those are common emotions. Although it contains some of my own feelings, it is definitely not a proper notebook-style essay. Calling it miscellaneous essays is fine, but calling it a notebook-style essay is a bit inappropriate. During this year, I did write ten kinds of aesthetically pleasing impressionistic essays like "Autumn Landscape Painting," a total of four articles, and some nostalgic essays, but I always felt that they were either too affected or too artificial, or the emotions were monotonous and stiff. These kinds of miscellaneous essays are more natural. When writing this type of miscellaneous essay, my state of mind is always common, and my attitude is always serious! This kind of commonness is perhaps nothing more than the commonness of birth.

My state of mind is common. Therefore, the collection is named "Common Collection" (平凡集). I hope that I can make my state of mind even more common.

Written after illness on the vernal equinox of 1936

Spring City Where Flowers Fly Everywhere 205

Yellow Wind 206

— Zang Kejia

My home is on the coast of the East Sea, enjoying the moistening effect of the marine air currents. Even in the slightly dry spring, I don't feel the threat of the wind. In March, the spring rain seems to be urging the flowers to bloom. If there is wind, it should be "the willow wind that brushes the face without causing coldness."

Since coming to this ancient city, I have come to know the yellow wind.

In this part of northern Shandong, there are no mountains. One can sweep the horizon for a thousand miles. There are no barriers between it and northern China, so it is suitable for the wind to come and go as if entering an uninhibited place.

People encircled in this ancient city cannot easily distinguish the boundaries of the seasons, because still within its embrace are clumps of weeds like yellow flowers, next to broken bricks and tiles mixed with white bones, and then stretches of open land, with a few families scattered on the edges of the land. The circle of the ancient city does not let the spring colors in. The trees are sparse. Spring here never seems like spring.

However, if you want to know the news of spring, it is not difficult. Just use the yellow wind as a marker. There is no ambiguity at all. The yellow wind seems to have an inextricable bond with spring. It will never forget her. It is afraid that youth cannot bear the loneliness.

Last year, because of the drought, the yellow wind was particularly severe. It has such great power that just thinking about it immediately makes people think of the instability of the universe! Its arrival is not fixed at any time, during the day, or perhaps in the night. You are sleeping soundly, and suddenly someone is shaking the doors and windows violently. You wake up abruptly, your heart pounding. At this time, the outside sounds like waves rising on the sea, like countless spirits roaring. When you realize what the sound is, you feel a bit suffocated in your nostrils. Clench your teeth, and there is a rustling sound. Close your eyes and you can't sleep anymore. A kind of terror engulfs your heart, as if you are in a dangerous atmosphere, afraid to think about the sun in the morning.

Opening your eyes in the morning, the small house has become another world. You are no longer the master. The tablecloth, window sill, books... are all sealed with dust. Opening the door, the wind and dust choke you back. It is raining outside. A rain of dust. The windows and doors shake pitifully like madmen. Fine sand finds a little gap and desperately drills into the house. I don't know where the sun has been blown. You can't see the sky, you can't see the ground, the universe has become a sea of soil! People and everything rise and fall in its waves, trying hard to root their feet in the ground. If you relax, you worry that a hand will grab you away. The branches are like ten thousand mosquitos struggling to fly into the sky, and it seems like something is tripping you under your feet, listening to its angry roar!

Lying on the bed with my eyes closed, I think of the quiet scenery of spring in my hometown to calm my swaying heart. "Wham," a clod of mud the size of a fist falls near my ear. I jump up suddenly, push open the door forcefully, and call the swirling current to rush into Shen Ting's house, because I am too worried about her sick body.

She is coughing in the house with a sad face. As soon as she sees me, she complains: "I told you not to be in this place"! After she finishes speaking, she coughs again, spitting out something red. I hug her and go to the training office to take refuge, because that room has double-layer glass windows.

The people seeking refuge are already full. Everyone has a handkerchief in their mouth, and apricot yellow is dotted on their hair and eyebrows. Putting her on a recliner, covering her face with a handkerchief, we look at each other, no one says a word. What can be used to compare this desolate taste?

Once, the red outside the glass window looked like it was on fire, with a buzzing sound. Once, it was all black, with no houses, no people, no shadows, no universe.

The sand dunes of northern China are uprooting and heading south. Every life has the terror of the end of the world. Looking at Shen Ting's appearance, I resentfully think: "Who told you to be attached to this sandy land without spring"?

Like an angry person gradually calming down, the wind becomes so small that it makes people think that the universe is worth cherishing. The window also turns white. This group of refugees removes their masks, removes the terror from their faces, pats their bodies, and pushes open the door of the house. At this time, the ground outside is like a white mirror in high places, and a pile of weeds and a pile of white sand in low places. A gentle breeze is still teasing them to spin around.

Everyone returns to their own house to sweep away three inches of dust and temporarily become the master again. But who dares to say that tomorrow will not come again?

The Night is Not Yet Over 207

In the Alley 208

— Shen Shengshi

Living in an alley, the days are extremely lonely. Usually, I have no other way to pass the time except reading.

A life of seclusion gradually makes a person's energy tend towards boredom. In poverty and embarrassment, all hope turns dark before my eyes.

In a deathly silent environment, life is easy to decline; like a piece of iron that easily rusts in damp air.

The weather has changed several times. However, I am still living in the alley with a dark mood, without any hope.

Sitting by the window, listening to the sound of reading from the neighbor's private school; the calls of vendors from the alley; the sounds of mothers-in-law and daughters-in-law scolding each other in nearby houses; and the rogue vagrants walking along the alley, straightening their throats and humming Peking opera. All of this causes me unreasonable discomfort. At noon and in the afternoon, the alley seems a little more lively. Elementary school students from nearby elementary schools come and go in the alley, and in the chaotic footsteps, two or three elementary school students sing songs. I can also hear the vigorous sound of the elementary school teacher's leather shoes hitting the alley.

One day passes, always silent tea and meals, a somber mood: foolishly lost in thought.

At dusk, the alley becomes quiet, leaving only the gasping coughs of old passersby. In front of the window, I look at the gray twilight clouds filled with coldness, and flocks of crows cawing and forming a black battle formation, then circling in the sky for exercises.

I am tired, how can I live like this forever; a low sigh scatters in the wind.

In a state of hopelessness and without comfort, the greatness and true meaning of life will gradually become blurred and dim in one's heart.

Under the light, accompanied by my elderly grandmother, I just think blankly about a life without any reliance; I begin to experience a kind of unbearable feeling of not being able to cry; the sadness of being rejected by the world, like thousands of sharp needles, piercing my painful heart.

I hope there will be a good dream at night, but in the dream, I am still walking in a dark alley, with a depressing gray rainy sky... Reading and writing are just a bleak way for a loser to pass the time!

I don't know when I will cheer up, move, and leave the life in the alley.

"Skill" 209

— Cao Juren

Lu Ji's "Rhyme Prose on Literature" (文賦) spoke of many experiences regarding the benefits and drawbacks of writing, and then suddenly shifted to say: "As for the abundant composition and flowing expression, adapting to circumstances and subtly expressing emotions... It is like a dancer responding to the rhythm by throwing their sleeves, and a singer responding to the strings with their voice. This is something a wheelwright cannot express, and thus cannot be fully explained by flowery words." This is also his experience. He always felt that literary creation has such a realm of "skill" that can be understood intuitively but not expressed in words. The pre-Qin philosophers talked a lot about this subtle and complex realm of "skill." Mencius and his disciples mentioned the word "skill" twice when discussing learning. One place said: "Wisdom is like skill; sagacity is like strength. It is like shooting at a target a hundred steps away; reaching the target is your strength, but hitting the target is not your strength." Another place said: "Carpenters and wheelwrights can give people rules, but they cannot make people skillful." Other stories, such as Zhuangzi's Cook Ding dismembering an ox, Wheelwright Bian's new wheels, and Lü's Spring and Autumn Annals' Yi Zhi discussing tripods, also explain this principle. (The Heavenly Ways chapter: "Wheelwright Bian said to Duke Huan, 'Judging from my craft, making wheels, if the chisel is too slow, it's loose and not strong; if it's too fast, it's rough and doesn't fit; neither slow nor fast, it's mastered by the hand and responds to the heart, it cannot be spoken, there's a principle in between, I cannot teach my son, my son cannot learn from me, so I'm seventy years old and still making wheels.'") Generally speaking, discussing literature and the Dao, reaching the deepest realm, these words can mutually illuminate and confirm each other. Mr. Yu Pingbo once expressed this idea and wrote an article about the wandering and solitude of literature. The passage in the preface to "Six Records of a Floating Life" (浮生六記) says it well:

"There is a common rule for the perfection of literary and career achievements, which is 'Seeking it will not necessarily get it, not seeking it may come naturally.' The most wonderful thing is to learn from the flowing water, the most wonderful thing is to learn from the spring birds and autumn insects. It is certainly not intentional, but it is not necessarily unintentional... When we encounter all external things, we should not be deliberate, deliberation leads to stagnation; we should not sever connections, severance leads to separation."

I don't want to repeat the opinions of my predecessors and explain the word "skill" in another roundabout way. What I am asking is, since it is so ingenious and subtle, that it cannot be spoken, as they say; then why do they keep talking and talking, never ceasing? I think their purpose is still to "obtain the transmission," but they are afraid that it is "impossible to transmit," so they try to find a path to "what can be spoken" from "what cannot be spoken." Therefore, they use "the wonderful cannot be spoken" to explain "the wonderful." In this regard, I think there are roughly three layers of meaning that can be said.

First, they (whether discussing metaphysics or art criticism) see that the root cause of most people's problems lies in being trapped in the barrier of words and unable to get out. Originally, it was "people" using "words," but the result is that "words" dominate "people." Therefore, a sharp rebuke is necessary, as Zhuangzi said: "What the world values in the Dao is books; books are nothing but words, and words have what is valued in them. What is valued in words is the meaning, and the meaning follows something. What the meaning follows cannot be transmitted in words. But the world values the transmission of words and books, even if the world values them, they are not worthy of being valued, because they value what is not worth valuing. Therefore, what can be seen is form and color, what can be heard is name and sound. Alas! People think that form, color, name, and sound are enough to obtain their feelings; but form, color, name, and sound are not enough to obtain their feelings, then the wise do not speak, and those who speak do not know. How can the world understand this!" (Guo Xiang's commentary clarifies this meaning, saying: "The words and meaning have something, and what the words and meaning refer to has nothing; therefore, seek it outside of the words and meaning, enter the realm of no words and no meaning, and then arrive.") We use language and words as tools to express emotions and ideas, but Zhuangzi tells us to seek it outside of the words and meaning. This has a very deep meaning; in modern terms, it is what Angellier said: "The words in poetry are only like stepping stones lying across a stream, we can walk over the stream on them. But if you just linger on them and don't move, your feet will inevitably get wet; you must hurry across!" Breaking the barrier of words is the only way to avoid the constraints of words; knowing that "skill" is within and outside of language and words is the only way to understand where "skill" lies. Mr. Zhang Taiyan said of his own learning, "Starting with analyzing concepts and ending with discarding concepts." It can also be used to discuss literature.

Second, the subtle realm of "skill" is originally "dim and vague," but this realm does not exist in a void, but in our experience. Although we cannot directly point to this realm with language and words, we can use other methods to guide everyone into this realm. Lu Ji's "Rhyme Prose on Literature" says about our creative imagination: "Floating in the abyss to drift with the current, washing the lower springs and secretly immersing; thus, submerging words that are displeasing, as if a fish is hooked and comes out, measuring the depth of the abyss, floating algae linked together, as if a soaring bird is shot down and falls from the high clouds." He thought that finding a suitable adjective or adverb, arranging a suitable set of words, was the same as shooting birds in the air or fishing in the abyss, not too early, not too late, finding it at the right time and place, this is called "skill." Mr. Zhou Zuoren talked about wine and said, "The method and tools for making wine seem simple, but the technique of cooking is extremely difficult; usually families who make wine hire a person, commonly called 'wine head worker,' to be in charge of identifying the timing of cooking the wine. It is said that this is not difficult, just go to the vat and bend down to listen, and hear the sound of bubbles inside, murmuring, like crabs spitting foam, then take it out to cook; a little early, the wine is not yet made, a little late, it turns sour. But how to determine the exact timing, others still cannot know, only experienced ears can determine, just like the eyes of antique experts distinguish antiquities." This can also be borrowed as an explanation of "skill." The meaning of "skill" exists universally. Being able to understand other "skills" also means understanding "skill" in creation; not appealing to metaphysics, but appealing to everyone's experience, this is the second layer.

Third, as the saying goes, "Practice makes perfect." Yang Xiong replied to Huan Tan's discussion of writing rhyme prose, saying: "Practice subdues the multitude of spirits, skill is nothing more than the gate of practice." The famous general Han Qi always hit the target with every shot, and an old oil vendor beside him ridiculed, saying: "It's just that your hand is hot." It can be seen that "skill" is not unobtainable, much practice can make you understand and do it. Koizumi Yakumo said: "When emotion comes, what happens? This is a moment of surprise, fear, pain, or pleasure, the prickling sensation, coming without a trace, going without a trace... No one can write this feeling on paper immediately, just as they received it. This can only be achieved through hard work... This process is very similar to focusing a telescope. Before a distant object can be clearly seen, the lens barrel must be rotated in a little, rotated out a little, then rotated in a little, rotated out a little, such extension and shortening, repeated adjustment. Yes, writers must use language like tourists use telescopes. This is the first necessary condition for any literary work." Literary "skill" cannot be obtained by departing from rules; carpenters and wheelwrights give people rules, which is the initial step to giving people skill. Xu Yinfang's postscript to Sikong Tu's "Discourse on Poetry with Li Sheng" says: "Biao Sheng discusses the flavor of poetry being outside of sour and salty, and then uses Youcheng's Suzhou as a standard, this is the high standard of poets, those who do not learn it well will easily fall into empty patterns. Among the Tang people, the four families of Wang, Meng, Wei, and Liu have similar poetic styles, and their poems are all obtained from hard work. People only see their clarity, elegance, and exquisiteness, but do not know that they have been washed and refined many times before achieving clarity, and refined through many tempering before achieving exquisiteness. If scholars seek it from the appearance of clarity and exquisiteness, they will inevitably imitate their tone and copy their words, and none will not fall into empty patterns." This is very well said. Clarity and exquisiteness come from tempering and refining, obtaining sagacity from foolishness, and obtaining skill from clumsiness, and then "thinking is more than half done."

Zhuangzi's "Achieving Life" chapter says, "Confucius went to Chu and came out of the forest, and saw a hunchback catching cicadas, as if picking them up. Confucius said, 'Are you skillful? Do you have a way?' He said, 'I have a way, in the fifth and sixth months, I stack the balls of clay to put on the end of the stick to catch the cicadas. If I miss, it is just the weight of a small silver coin. If I stack three and don't miss, then I miss once in ten. If I stack five and don't miss, I pick them up. I stand like a tree trunk, and I hold my arm like a dry branch, although the heaven and earth are big, and there are many things, I only know the cicada's wing. I don't turn or lean, I don't exchange the cicada's wing for anything, why can't I get it!' Confucius turned to his disciples and said, 'Using the will without distraction, then it is concentrated in the spirit, is this not what the hunchback elder says?'" I use this story as the ending to explain skill; truly, there is no other way to treat the aphid but to catch it diligently.

Page 17

Supplement to the Shanghai Newspaper

Talking Points

Mother Education Competition 210

— Zhou Ge

The Shanghai Women's Education Hall on Hua Long Road in the French Concession, in order to promote the sense of responsibility of mothers in the family and create a social atmosphere that values virtuous mothers, specifically held a Mother Education Competition on Children's Day, April 4th. Participating children must be accompanied by their mothers. The competition items are divided into physique, cleanliness, etiquette, and communication, etc.

I think this work is very important, but it is also very wasteful. How do I say this? It makes me think of a film from Lianhua Film Company in the past called "Little Angel." The film depicted two families, one family with a very good "virtuous mother atmosphere," and the other the opposite, where the mother gambled all day, so that the child's "cleanliness," "etiquette," etc., were not as good as the child raised under the "virtuous mother education." So, if the Women's Education Hall can promote "mother education" among this group of women, it might not be a bad thing.

However, this is a wasteful thing! Why? First, are women only supposed to give birth to children and spend their whole lives working on their children's "physique," "cleanliness," "etiquette," and "communication," etc.? Although these things should not be said to be the responsibility of mothers, aren't they also the responsibility of fathers? To put it more broadly, creating a good child is not only the great responsibility of mothers and fathers, but also the even greater responsibility of society. Even if you as parents devote all your energy to educating children, the education of the social environment will later turn your energy into nothing. Second: Mothers themselves are also a problem. Apart from those ladies who want to create a "virtuous mother atmosphere," we see countless broad, hardworking women whose own "cleanliness" and "physique," etc., are still a problem, so how can they take care of their children's "physique" and "etiquette"?

Because of these two points, I think this is a wasteful move. However, among those ladies with a "virtuous mother atmosphere," it is a more worthwhile "big event"!

Life 211

— Lin Jia

Even in winter, the children in the countryside wake up with the dawn. And since country folk don’t consider children's play a serious matter, every day in the freezing morning, a group of children would come knocking on the school door. At this time, I would put on my clothes and pull open the bolt for them, letting that group of children with their heads buried in fur hats run into the dark classroom. Then, a burnt smell of poorly burnt wood and the scent of burnt chaff would seep into my bedroom. Because the winter in the north is extremely cold, and a classroom left empty overnight is more freezing than an ordinary house, and the school doesn't have the funds for a stove, each of them would hold a gray fire pot, filled with broken charcoal? Or something like chaff, placing it on their desks. Thus, the three small classrooms would maintain a bit of pitiful warmth amidst an not-so-pleasant smell. The classroom and the teacher's room are connected, with the door opening in the wall between them, making it seem like a suite of the classroom. So, as the grayish-white little fire pots were brought into the classroom one by one, I also smelled the unique scent of rural homes in winter.

At this time, I would leave the heated brick bed that took up half of the small room and sit at a large square table in front of the window, waiting for the old man who was both the night watchman and the school handyman to bring me water to wash my face. Outside, the children in the classroom would read their books aloud.

After the washing water was brought, the old man would pour a pot of boiling water into a round, big-bellied red clay teapot and put firewood burned while boiling water into a gray fire pot, bringing it to my room. After all of this was done, after a while, I would need to check the time, pick up the bell and ring it twice in my room, then put down the bell, pick up the roll book, textbooks, and chalk box, and run to the small platform.

The classroom was narrow and long, with only three windows with rustling paper stretched over them, set into the front wall. The room seemed a bit damp. In the center, there were several rows of crude, unfinished white wooden desks and benches. In this dim and rough environment, there sat twenty-six or twenty-seven rural wild children who were quite a match for the classroom. The characteristic of these children was that they constantly had two streams of snot running down their noses, frequently wiping them with their sleeves that had become shiny. Even more were "slapping" along in two pairs of worn straw shoes with broken heels, bravely running in the ankle-deep snowy fields on snowy days. The only two girls still had bound feet, dragging along and walking with a twist in their small braids. The teaching method was naturally multi-grade, dividing the twenty-six or twenty-seven children into fragmented small groups, and the teacher’s focus was also divided into fragments. While teaching, there would often be coughing old men, holding dry tobacco pipes, coming in to watch the fun, sometimes even helping the teacher loudly discipline their own children. At such times, I could only force a bitter smile or try to smooth things over because the old men were all people of status in the village and were not allowed to be openly interfered with.

When the winter sun was close to the ground, it was often the time when the last review was finished. Then, the silent village would suddenly become lively, filled with the shouts of children. I would let out a sigh and collapse onto the earthen bed, along with my fatigue. Soon, in the quiet courtyard, a familiar sound of footsteps could be heard. In the small room filled with shadows, the man holding the meal would appear. The meal was contracted to a farmer's family for five silver dollars, taken from the seventeen silver dollar salary. We often ate millet pancakes or black bread, small tofu, very thick porridge, and a small dish of stir-fried vegetables especially for the "teacher."

After eating, the old man who was both the night watchman and the school handyman would again bring a basket of grass to burn for my heated brick bed. After it was burned and the whole room was filled with smoke, he would cough and take the empty basket away. Looking at his limping back as he walked away, it often made people feel an indescribable loneliness. Only this little bit of time belonged to me, but it was often taken away, because who knows when an old man with a long pipe would stride in to chat, or a stranger would come in, holding two red paper strips, wanting me to read their "eight characters," or clutching a yellow paper, wanting me to write a "document" for them. When I told them with a bitter smile that I couldn't do this kind of work, they would often stare with a pair of confused eyes, the meaning probably being: How can a teacher not do such a small thing? Or they would ramble on with me, saying that the previous teachers all wrote them.

Knowing that a few words of explanation would be useless, I could only send them away with a bitter smile. Watching their clumsy shadows disappear into the darkness, I would be confused and think about their sons, thinking about how to teach their sons.

The Eight Great Hutongs 212

— Zhu Lu

— Recollections of Beiping

Late at night, I followed a friend out of Qianmen, winding through narrow alleys, walking from this hutong to that hutong, my feet stepping on the uneven cobblestone road. A dark hutong unfolded before me.

Stepping into another large hutong, it was much brighter. Each door had a glowing electric light, red and green ribbons, lined with glass frames, with many names on them. Pieces of red characters seemed to dance before my eyes.

I followed, walking in the Eight Great Hutongs. I felt like I was walking in circles in a maze. From this hutong, turning to that hutong, there were only lanterns and rows of open black-lacquered red-lettered gates.

Going in through this doorframe, and then coming out of this doorframe, I followed, stepping into the first-class brothels, then to the second-class teahouses, I followed, dizzy.

Every time I walked into an open door, into a room with a lot of furniture, a plump mama-san, like a judge, stood like a wooden bucket, loudly calling out the charming names of the girls, names just like those in ancient Chinese legends, Spring, Summer, Autumn, Winter, Moon, Round, Flower, Fragrant, Beautiful, Gorgeous...

One by one, the girls stepped into the threshold, turned around and came back, each bringing a burst of powdery scent, one after another, long, round, different faces, floated before me.

Again, stepping into a door of another house, into a narrow room, the furniture inside became dilapidated and crude, the room was so old, I felt a little strange.

In the loud shouting of the mama-san, one by one the girls came out, one after another, I was startled, drowsily as if waking up from a dream.

The white face painted with water powder like a white wall *blank space* different color, tall

— Illustrations by Wan Chao Chen, Explanation by Xin Xin

Krogstad: I came home and saw the note you left. What is this all about?

Mrs. Linde: We must talk.

Krogstad: Is there anything left for us to talk about? Since you left me, it's as if the ground I stood on has sunk. Look at me now, I've become like a shipwrecked person grabbing onto a broken plank.

Mrs. Linde: I am also a shipwrecked person grabbing onto a broken plank. Neither remembering nor caring for anyone. Krogstad, what if we two shipwrecked people support each other, what do you think?

Krogstad: Do you really mean it? Do you know all the bad things I've done in the past?

Mrs. Linde: You seemed to say earlier that if you had me back then, you would never have ended up in this state.

Krogstad: You naturally don't know the means I used to deal with the Helmer couple?

Mrs. Linde: I know everything.

Krogstad: I wish I could undo this. I will wait for Helmer to return here,

And ask him to return the letter.

Mrs. Linde: No, Helmer should know about this secret loan. The two of them should be completely honest with each other. This hesitant approach will never lead to a day of openness.

Krogstad: Alright. But if I can help, I will do it immediately. I will wait for you across the street and send you home.

Storytelling 217

Cai Xiaofang's Mao Family Book

Zhongxi (1040) 1:00 PM to 1:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Jia Baoyu Also Talks About Xiaoxiang Pavilion"

Severe winter frost forms into ice. The moonlight is hazy and about to break the soul. A gust of north wind penetrates the bones. The Black, cavernous Grand View Garden is cold and desolate. Baoyu is walking all the way on Flower Street. The night is late and quiet, with no sound. He is a lamp. Alone. Dark shadows advancing forward. All alone he comes to Xiaoxiang Pavilion. To see if the illness of sister Lin has lessened. Gently knocks the copper ring with a dripping sound. Is there anyone who will quickly open the door? Zixuan listens. Asks: Is Second Master wishing to come inside? She busily opens the door. Please be careful of the cold of the deep night, have no mercy. Thank you sister for being so considerate. I will never forget your great kindness. Only for being worried about your Miss Lin. That is why, in the quiet of the night, I have come. Walking, I have already arrived at the bedside. Seeing her, she is gasping for breath with tears streaming down. One moment calling "Sister Lin". One moment calling his "Cousin". Her almond eyes slightly open and cannot see clearly. Cousin, this aunt in your house is too harsh to me. Her words are absurd, creating right and wrong. Although the old grandmother loves me. It is a pity I cannot please the previous husband with peace. The karmic debt from a previous life has been settled in this life. Please don't look at this ill-fated person any more. Sister, cast away all your worries. You must not look down on yourself too much. I advise you to eat and drink three meals a day. Add clothes to keep your body warm. I advise you to sleep early at night, not too late. You must drink more decoctions. I advise you not to listen to the words of the sisters. They seem false, like a play, yet also like truth. I advise you to take care of your body and mind, and cherish yourself. Never think again of the old family home in Yangzhou. Hearing these words, tears streamed down. You wretch, you are most attentive to me. Cousin, please return to the Yihong Courtyard soon. Tears have soaked through the perfumed silk handkerchief. This body is not necessarily too drifting and rootless.

Xu Wenbi's Opening Chapter

Hangye 1180 5:30 PM to 12:45 PM

Opening Chapter "Arranged Marriage"

Seeing the kind face in the White Cloud Nunnery. Miss is, the news is vague, adding to the hatred. The aunt is, the evening drum and morning bell mark the years. Suffering the cold and indifferent words of the snobbish nuns. Suddenly, anger fills my chest. I order the housekeeper to be diligent and respectful in the future. Still, the lady of the Western Courtyard must be kept in the dark. Listen, I hear the sound of agreeing to each instruction. From now on, let the lady settle in. However, grieving for her son, her pain is doubled. That is, Old Madam Bi has ten thousand points of sorrow. Love binds the children. Only because the selection of imperial consorts is extremely strict according to imperial order. I pity the girls who are yet to be married. Nurturing them like flowers for eighteen years. Moreover, her temperament is gentle and her appearance is dignified. Her qin playing does not yield to Ban Ji's wisdom. Praising her weeping catkins is like praising Tao Wenxian. Wanting to select a dragon steed is difficult to satisfy. Only, the Fang family's young master is most elegant. Consulting with both sons to temporarily recruit a son-in-law. Mother, he is, the one with whom Zong Biao Songting made a previous agreement. Who knew that the lady would not adopt it at all. At once she writes a marriage agreement in the style of a flower note. Came to the plum blossom study and diligently invited her. Sitting behind the screen shoulder to shoulder with her sister-in-law. Want to call her face.

Film

A Great Drought 219

"The Lost Lamb" Because they had to film a drought scene, the idyllic Huacun has recently transformed to present an extremely arid scene. Not only have the flowers, plants, and fruit trees in front of the village lost their vibrant color, but even the green river that surrounds the village has dried up and is full of cracks.

This setting fully expresses the air of rural areas suffering from drought, but such a setting can only be created with a lot of manpower, time, and money. To speak only of the river, which is more than eighty feet wide, to dry the river, the water must be pumped out. To pump the water, piles must first be driven and dams built. The scale of this project, including dam building and pumping water with machines, can be imagined. However, after spending so much time and money, what will be shown on the screen in the future will only be a shot of forty feet, projected on the screen for only three seconds. If we calculate it, the cost of these forty feet of film cannot be said to be inexpensive.

However, because of this dam building and water pumping, the workers caught more than ten pounds of fish to eat.

Han Langan and Liu Jiqun Break Up 220

Xinhua Company Completes a Good Deed

I remember when it was rumored in Hollywood that Laurel and Hardy were going to break up, many fans stood up to express their opposition and seemed very indignant. This is because the plays they collaborated on left too deep an impression on the fans; if they wanted to break up, the fans would not agree.

In China, Han Langan and Liu Jiqun were long recognized as the Laurel and Hardy of the East, and they were also warmly supported by fans. But unfortunately, Liu Jiqun terminated his contract with Lianhua, and Han Langan was immediately isolated. The Laurel of the East, the Laurel and Hardy of the East, also had a breakup, which is really a piece of news that fans will find very unpleasant. But not to disappoint you, Xinhua Company has now come out to complete this good deed. The recent Xinhua film "Peach Blossom Spring Dream" is a new type of comedy in which Han Langan and Liu Jiqun are cast as the main characters. The director is Yang Xiaozhong, and he plans to make you laugh to tears in the theater, with a large number of jokes from beginning to end that you cannot help but laugh at; at the same time, attention is paid to other roles, and the female leads include Tong Yuejuan and Xu Manli, etc., who were universally praised in the past films "Peach Blossom Fan" and "Song of Everlasting Regret".

Now, Laurel and Hardy have not broken up, and our Han Langan and Liu Jiqun's collaboration on "Peach Blossom Spring Dream" at Xinhua Company is already half finished.

Paris Releases "Sergeant York" in Advance 221

The historical war epic "Sergeant York," starring Gary Cooper, leading more than 3,000 people, which broke the box office record of the Great Light Theater, is indeed an unprecedented feat. Movie fans in West Shanghai have sent letters and telegrams requesting the Paris Theater to release it in advance during the spring vacation. In particular, students have made the most enthusiastic requests. The Paris authorities could not refuse the favor, so they had to make the premiere in West Shanghai starting today. I hope the audience will pay attention to it.
